::: {#section-5.6 .section}
### [5.6.](#section-5.6){.section-number .selfRef} [Comments and Remarks](#name-comments-and-remarks-2){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-comments-and-remarks-2}

Lost packets represent a challenge for delay variation metrics. See
[Section
4.1](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc3393#section-4.1){.relref} of
\[[RFC3393](#RFC3393){.xref}\] and the delay variation applicability
statement \[[RFC5481](#RFC5481){.xref}\] for extensive analysis and
comparison of PDV and an alternate metric, IPDV (Inter-Packet Delay
Variation).[¶](#section-5.6-1){.pilcrow}
:::
:::
:::

::: {#dns_response_latency_and_loss}
::: {#section-6 .section}
## [6.](#section-6){.section-number .selfRef} [DNS Response Latency and Loss Registry Entries](#name-dns-response-latency-and-lo){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-dns-response-latency-and-lo}

This section gives initial Registry Entries for DNS Response Latency and
Loss from a network user\'s perspective, for a specific named resource.
The metric can be measured repeatedly for different named resources.
\[[RFC2681](#RFC2681){.xref}\] defines a round-trip delay metric. We
build on that metric by specifying several of the input Parameters to
precisely define two metrics for measuring DNS latency and
loss.[¶](#section-6-1){.pilcrow}

All column entries besides the ID, Name, Description, and Output
Reference Method categories are the same; thus, this section defines two
closely related Registry Entries. As a result, IANA has assigned
corresponding URLs to each of the two Named
Metrics.[¶](#section-6-2){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-6.1 .section}
### [6.1.](#section-6.1){.section-number .selfRef} [Summary](#name-summary-3){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-summary-3}

This category includes multiple indexes to the Registry Entries: the
element ID and Metric Name.[¶](#section-6.1-1){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-6.1.1 .section}
#### [6.1.1.](#section-6.1.1){.section-number .selfRef} [ID (Identifier)](#name-id-identifier-3){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-id-identifier-3}

IANA has allocated the numeric Identifiers 4 and 5 for the two Named
Metric Entries in [Section 6](#dns_response_latency_and_loss){.xref}.
See [Section 6.1.2](#name612){.xref} for mapping to
Names.[¶](#section-6.1.1-1){.pilcrow}
:::

::: {#name612}
::: {#section-6.1.2 .section}
#### [6.1.2.](#section-6.1.2){.section-number .selfRef} [Name](#name-name-3){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-name-3}

[]{.break}

4:
:   RTDNS_Active_IP-UDP-Poisson_RFC8912sec6_Seconds_Raw[¶](#section-6.1.2-1.2){.pilcrow}
:   

5:
:   RLDNS_Active_IP-UDP-Poisson_RFC8912sec6_Logical_Raw[¶](#section-6.1.2-1.4){.pilcrow}
:   
:::
:::

::: {#section-6.1.3 .section}
#### [6.1.3.](#section-6.1.3){.section-number .selfRef} [URI](#name-uri-3){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-uri-3}

URL:
<https://www.iana.org/assignments/performance-metrics/RTDNS_Active_IP-UDP-Poisson_RFC8912sec6_Seconds_Raw>[¶](#section-6.1.3-1){.pilcrow}

URL:
<https://www.iana.org/assignments/performance-metrics/RLDNS_Active_IP-UDP-Poisson_RFC8912sec6_Logical_Raw>[¶](#section-6.1.3-2){.pilcrow}
:::

::: {#section-6.1.4 .section}
#### [6.1.4.](#section-6.1.4){.section-number .selfRef} [Description](#name-description-3){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-description-3}

This is a metric for DNS Response performance from a network user\'s
perspective, for a specific named resource. The metric can be measured
repeatedly using different resource
names.[¶](#section-6.1.4-1){.pilcrow}

[]{.break}

RTDNS:
:   This metric assesses the response time, the interval from the query
    transmission to the response.[¶](#section-6.1.4-2.2){.pilcrow}
:   

RLDNS:
:   This metric indicates that the response was deemed lost. In other
    words, the response time exceeded the maximum waiting
    time.[¶](#section-6.1.4-2.4){.pilcrow}
:   
:::

::: {#section-6.1.5 .section}
#### [6.1.5.](#section-6.1.5){.section-number .selfRef} [Change Controller](#name-change-controller-3){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-change-controller-3}

IETF[¶](#section-6.1.5-1){.pilcrow}
:::

::: {#section-6.1.6 .section}
#### [6.1.6.](#section-6.1.6){.section-number .selfRef} [Version (of Registry Format)](#name-version-of-registry-format-3){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-version-of-registry-format-3}

1.0[¶](#section-6.1.6-1){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#section-6.2 .section}
### [6.2.](#section-6.2){.section-number .selfRef} [Metric Definition](#name-metric-definition-3){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-metric-definition-3}

This category includes columns to prompt the entry of all necessary
details related to the metric definition, including the RFC reference
and values of input factors, called \"Fixed
Parameters\".[¶](#section-6.2-1){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-6.2.1 .section}
#### [6.2.1.](#section-6.2.1){.section-number .selfRef} [Reference Definition](#name-reference-definition-5){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-reference-definition-5}

For Delay:[¶](#section-6.2.1-1){.pilcrow}

Mockapetris, P., \"Domain names - implementation and specification\",
STD 13, RFC 1035, DOI 10.17487/RFC1035, November 1987,
\<https://www.rfc-editor.org/info/rfc1035> (and updates).
\[[RFC1035](#RFC1035){.xref}\][¶](#section-6.2.1-2){.pilcrow}

Almes, G., Kalidindi, S., and M. Zekauskas, \"A Round-trip Delay Metric
for IPPM\", RFC 2681, DOI 10.17487/RFC2681, September 1999,
\<https://www.rfc-editor.org/info/rfc2681>.
\[[RFC2681](#RFC2681){.xref}\][¶](#section-6.2.1-3){.pilcrow}

[Section
2.4](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc2681#section-2.4){.relref} of
\[[RFC2681](#RFC2681){.xref}\] provides the reference definition of the
singleton (single value) round-trip delay metric. [Section
3.4](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc2681#section-3.4){.relref} of
\[[RFC2681](#RFC2681){.xref}\] provides the reference definition
expanded to cover a multi-singleton sample. Note that terms such as
\"singleton\" and \"sample\" are defined in [Section
11](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc2330#section-11){.relref} of
\[[RFC2330](#RFC2330){.xref}\].[¶](#section-6.2.1-4){.pilcrow}

For DNS Response Latency, the entities in \[[RFC1035](#RFC1035){.xref}\]
must be mapped to \[[RFC2681](#RFC2681){.xref}\]. The Local Host with
its User Program and Resolver take the Role of \"Src\", and the Foreign
Name Server takes the Role of \"Dst\".[¶](#section-6.2.1-5){.pilcrow}

Note that although the definition of round-trip delay between the Source
(Src) and the Destination (Dst) at T as provided in [Section
2.4](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc2681#section-2.4){.relref} of
\[[RFC2681](#RFC2681){.xref}\] is directionally ambiguous in the text,
this metric tightens the definition further to recognize that the host
in the Src Role will send the first packet to the host in the Dst Role
and will ultimately receive the corresponding return packet from the Dst
(when neither is lost).[¶](#section-6.2.1-6){.pilcrow}

For Loss:[¶](#section-6.2.1-7){.pilcrow}

Morton, A., \"Round-Trip Packet Loss Metrics\", RFC 6673, DOI
10.17487/RFC6673, August 2012,
\<https://www.rfc-editor.org/info/rfc6673>.
\[[RFC6673](#RFC6673){.xref}\][¶](#section-6.2.1-8){.pilcrow}

For DNS Response Loss, the entities in \[[RFC1035](#RFC1035){.xref}\]
must be mapped to \[[RFC6673](#RFC6673){.xref}\]. The Local Host with
its User Program and Resolver take the Role of \"Src\", and the Foreign
Name Server takes the Role of \"Dst\".[¶](#section-6.2.1-9){.pilcrow}

Both response time and Loss metrics employ a maximum waiting time for
received responses, so the count of lost packets to total packets sent
is the basis for the loss determination as per [Section
4.3](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6673#section-4.3){.relref} of
\[[RFC6673](#RFC6673){.xref}\].[¶](#section-6.2.1-10){.pilcrow}
:::

::: {#section-6.2.2 .section}
#### [6.2.2.](#section-6.2.2){.section-number .selfRef} [Fixed Parameters](#name-fixed-parameters-3){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-fixed-parameters-3}

[]{.break}

Type-P as defined in [Section 13](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc2330#section-13){.relref} of \[[RFC2330](#RFC2330){.xref}\]:
:   []{.break}

    IPv4 header values:
    :   []{.break}

        DSCP:
        :   Set to 0[¶](#section-6.2.2-1.2.2.2.2.2){.pilcrow}
        :   

        TTL:
        :   Set to 255[¶](#section-6.2.2-1.2.2.2.2.4){.pilcrow}
        :   

        Protocol:
        :   Set to 17 (UDP)[¶](#section-6.2.2-1.2.2.2.2.6){.pilcrow}
        :   
    :   

    []{.break}

    IPv6 header values:
    :   []{.break}

        DSCP:
        :   Set to 0[¶](#section-6.2.2-1.2.3.2.2.2){.pilcrow}
        :   

        Hop Count:
        :   Set to 255[¶](#section-6.2.2-1.2.3.2.2.4){.pilcrow}
        :   

        Next Header:
        :   Set to 17 (UDP)[¶](#section-6.2.2-1.2.3.2.2.6){.pilcrow}
        :   

        Flow Label:
        :   Set to 0[¶](#section-6.2.2-1.2.3.2.2.8){.pilcrow}
        :   

        Extension Headers:
        :   None[¶](#section-6.2.2-1.2.3.2.2.10){.pilcrow}
        :   
    :   

    []{.break}

    UDP header values:
    :   []{.break}

        Source port:
        :   53[¶](#section-6.2.2-1.2.4.2.2.2){.pilcrow}
        :   

        Destination port:
        :   53[¶](#section-6.2.2-1.2.4.2.2.4){.pilcrow}
        :   

        Checksum:
        :   The checksum [MUST]{.bcp14} be calculated and the non-zero
            checksum included in the
            header[¶](#section-6.2.2-1.2.4.2.2.6){.pilcrow}
        :   
    :   

    []{.break}

    Payload:

    :   The payload contains a DNS message as defined in
        \[[RFC1035](#RFC1035){.xref}\] with the following
        values:[¶](#section-6.2.2-1.2.5.2.1){.pilcrow}

        []{.break}

        The DNS header section contains:
        :   []{.break}

            Identification (see the Runtime column)

            :   

            :   

            QR:
            :   Set to 0
                (Query)[¶](#section-6.2.2-1.2.5.2.2.2.2.4){.pilcrow}
            :   

            OPCODE:
            :   Set to 0 (standard
                query)[¶](#section-6.2.2-1.2.5.2.2.2.2.6){.pilcrow}
            :   

            AA:
            :   Not set[¶](#section-6.2.2-1.2.5.2.2.2.2.8){.pilcrow}
            :   

            TC:
            :   Not set[¶](#section-6.2.2-1.2.5.2.2.2.2.10){.pilcrow}
            :   

            RD:
            :   Set to 1 (recursion
                desired)[¶](#section-6.2.2-1.2.5.2.2.2.2.12){.pilcrow}
            :   

            RA:
            :   Not set[¶](#section-6.2.2-1.2.5.2.2.2.2.14){.pilcrow}
            :   

            RCODE:
            :   Not set[¶](#section-6.2.2-1.2.5.2.2.2.2.16){.pilcrow}
            :   

            QDCOUNT:
            :   Set to 1 (only one
                entry)[¶](#section-6.2.2-1.2.5.2.2.2.2.18){.pilcrow}
            :   

            ANCOUNT:
            :   Not set[¶](#section-6.2.2-1.2.5.2.2.2.2.20){.pilcrow}
            :   

            NSCOUNT:
            :   Not set[¶](#section-6.2.2-1.2.5.2.2.2.2.22){.pilcrow}
            :   

            ARCOUNT:
            :   Not set[¶](#section-6.2.2-1.2.5.2.2.2.2.24){.pilcrow}
            :   
        :   

        []{.break}

        The Question section contains:
        :   []{.break}

            QNAME:
            :   The Fully Qualified Domain Name (FQDN) provided as input
                for the test; see the Runtime
                column[¶](#section-6.2.2-1.2.5.2.3.2.2.2){.pilcrow}
            :   

            QTYPE:
            :   The query type provided as input for the test; see the
                Runtime
                column[¶](#section-6.2.2-1.2.5.2.3.2.2.4){.pilcrow}
            :   

            QCLASS:
            :   Set to 1 for
                IN[¶](#section-6.2.2-1.2.5.2.3.2.2.6){.pilcrow}
            :   
        :   

        []{.break}

        The other sections do not contain any Resource Records (RRs).

        :   

        :   

    :   
:   

[]{.break}

Other measurement Parameters:
:   []{.break}

    Tmax:
    :   A loss threshold waiting time (and to help disambiguate
        queries). The value is 5.0, expressed in units of seconds, as a
        positive value of type decimal64 with fraction digits = 4 (see
        [Section
        9.3](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6020#section-9.3){.relref}
        of \[[RFC6020](#RFC6020){.xref}\]) and with a resolution of
        0.0001 seconds (0.1 ms), with lossless conversion to/from the
        32-bit NTP timestamp as per [Section
        6](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc5905#section-6){.relref} of
        \[[RFC5905](#RFC5905){.xref}\].[¶](#section-6.2.2-2.2.2.2){.pilcrow}
    :   
:   

[]{.break}

Observation:
:   Reply packets will contain a DNS Response and may contain
    RRs.[¶](#section-6.2.2-3.2){.pilcrow}
:   
:::
:::

::: {#section-6.3 .section}
### [6.3.](#section-6.3){.section-number .selfRef} [Method of Measurement](#name-method-of-measurement-3){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-method-of-measurement-3}

This category includes columns for references to relevant sections of
the RFC(s) and any supplemental information needed to ensure an
unambiguous method for implementations.[¶](#section-6.3-1){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-6.3.1 .section}
#### [6.3.1.](#section-6.3.1){.section-number .selfRef} [Reference Methods](#name-reference-methods-3){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-reference-methods-3}

The methodology for this metric (equivalent to
Type-P-Round-trip-Delay-Poisson-Stream) is defined as in [Section
2.6](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc2681#section-2.6){.relref} of
\[[RFC2681](#RFC2681){.xref}\] (for singletons) and [Section
3.6](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc2681#section-3.6){.relref} of
\[[RFC2681](#RFC2681){.xref}\] (for samples) using the Type-P and
Timeout defined in the Fixed Parameters
column.[¶](#section-6.3.1-1){.pilcrow}

The reference method distinguishes between long-delayed packets and lost
packets by implementing a maximum waiting time for packet arrival. Tmax
is the waiting time used as the threshold to declare a response packet
lost. Lost packets [SHALL]{.bcp14} be designated as having undefined
delay and counted for the RLDNS metric.[¶](#section-6.3.1-2){.pilcrow}

The calculations on the delay (RTT) [SHALL]{.bcp14} be performed on the
conditional distribution, conditioned on successful packet arrival
within Tmax. Also, when all packet delays are stored, the process that
calculates the RTT value [MUST]{.bcp14} enforce the Tmax threshold on
stored values before calculations. See [Section
4.1](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc3393#section-4.1){.relref} of
\[[RFC3393](#RFC3393){.xref}\] for details on the conditional
distribution to exclude undefined values of delay, and see [Section
5](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6703#section-5){.relref} of
\[[RFC6703](#RFC6703){.xref}\] for background on this analysis
choice.[¶](#section-6.3.1-3){.pilcrow}

The reference method requires some way to distinguish between different
packets in a stream to establish correspondence between sending times
and receiving times for each successfully arriving
reply.[¶](#section-6.3.1-4){.pilcrow}

DNS messages bearing queries provide for random ID Numbers in the
Identification header field, so more than one query may be launched
while a previous request is outstanding when the ID Number is used.
Therefore, the ID Number [MUST]{.bcp14} be retained at the Src and
included with each response packet to disambiguate packet reordering if
it occurs.[¶](#section-6.3.1-5){.pilcrow}

If a DNS Response does not arrive within Tmax, the response time RTDNS
is undefined, and RLDNS = 1. The Message ID [SHALL]{.bcp14} be used to
disambiguate the successive queries that are otherwise
identical.[¶](#section-6.3.1-6){.pilcrow}

Since the ID Number field is only 16 bits in length, it places a limit
on the number of simultaneous outstanding DNS queries during a stress
test from a single Src address.[¶](#section-6.3.1-7){.pilcrow}

Refer to [Section
4.4](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6673#section-4.4){.relref} of
\[[RFC6673](#RFC6673){.xref}\] for an expanded discussion of the
instruction to \"send a Type-P packet back to the Src as quickly as
possible\" in [Section
2.6](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc2681#section-2.6){.relref} of
\[[RFC2681](#RFC2681){.xref}\]. However, the DNS server is expected to
perform all required functions to prepare and send a response, so the
response time will include processing time and network delay. [Section
8](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6673#section-8){.relref} of
\[[RFC6673](#RFC6673){.xref}\] presents additional requirements that
[SHALL]{.bcp14} be included in the Method of Measurement for this
metric.[¶](#section-6.3.1-8){.pilcrow}

In addition to operations described in \[[RFC2681](#RFC2681){.xref}\],
the Src [MUST]{.bcp14} parse the DNS headers of the reply and prepare
the query response information for subsequent reporting as a measured
result, along with the round-trip delay.[¶](#section-6.3.1-9){.pilcrow}
:::

::: {#section-6.3.2 .section}
#### [6.3.2.](#section-6.3.2){.section-number .selfRef} [Packet Stream Generation](#name-packet-stream-generation-3){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-packet-stream-generation-3}

This section provides details regarding packet traffic, which is used as
the basis for measurement. In IPPM Metrics, this is called the
\"stream\"; this stream can easily be described by providing the list of
stream Parameters.[¶](#section-6.3.2-1){.pilcrow}

[Section
11.1.3](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc2330#section-11.1.3){.relref}
of \[[RFC2330](#RFC2330){.xref}\] provides three methods to generate
Poisson sampling intervals. The reciprocal of lambda is the average
packet spacing; thus, the Runtime Parameter is
Reciprocal_lambda = 1⁠/lambda, in
seconds.[¶](#section-6.3.2-2){.pilcrow}

Method 3 [SHALL]{.bcp14} be used. Where given a start time (Runtime
Parameter), the subsequent send times are all computed prior to
measurement by computing the pseudorandom distribution of inter-packet
send times (truncating the distribution as specified in the Parameter
Trunc), and the Src sends each packet at the computed
times.[¶](#section-6.3.2-3){.pilcrow}

Note that Trunc is the upper limit on inter-packet times in the Poisson
distribution. A random value greater than Trunc is set equal to Trunc
instead.[¶](#section-6.3.2-4){.pilcrow}
:::

::: {#section-6.3.3 .section}
#### [6.3.3.](#section-6.3.3){.section-number .selfRef} [Traffic Filtering (Observation) Details](#name-traffic-filtering-observation){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-traffic-filtering-observation}

N/A[¶](#section-6.3.3-1){.pilcrow}
:::

::: {#section-6.3.4 .section}
#### [6.3.4.](#section-6.3.4){.section-number .selfRef} [Sampling Distribution](#name-sampling-distribution-3){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-sampling-distribution-3}

N/A[¶](#section-6.3.4-1){.pilcrow}
:::

::: {#section-6.3.5 .section}
#### [6.3.5.](#section-6.3.5){.section-number .selfRef} [Runtime Parameters and Data Format](#name-runtime-parameters-and-data-f){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-runtime-parameters-and-data-f}

Runtime Parameters are input factors that must be determined, configured
into the measurement system, and reported with the results for the
context to be complete.[¶](#section-6.3.5-1){.pilcrow}

[]{.break}

Src:
:   The IP address of the host in the Src Role (format
    ipv4‑address-no-zone value for IPv4 or ipv6-address-no-zone value
    for IPv6; see [Section
    4](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6991#section-4){.relref} of
    \[[RFC6991](#RFC6991){.xref}\]).[¶](#section-6.3.5-2.2){.pilcrow}
:   

Dst:
:   The IP address of the host in the Dst Role (format
    ipv4‑address-no-zone value for IPv4 or ipv6-address-no-zone value
    for IPv6; see [Section
    4](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6991#section-4){.relref} of
    \[[RFC6991](#RFC6991){.xref}\]).[¶](#section-6.3.5-2.4){.pilcrow}
:   

T0:
:   A time, the start of a measurement interval (format \"date‑time\" as
    specified in [Section
    5.6](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc3339#section-5.6){.relref} of
    \[[RFC3339](#RFC3339){.xref}\]; see also \"date‑and‑time\" in
    [Section
    3](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6991#section-3){.relref} of
    \[[RFC6991](#RFC6991){.xref}\]). The UTC Time Zone is required by
    [Section
    6.1](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc2330#section-6.1){.relref} of
    \[[RFC2330](#RFC2330){.xref}\]. When T0 is \"all-zeros\", a start
    time is unspecified and Tf is to be interpreted as the duration of
    the measurement interval. The start time is controlled through other
    means.[¶](#section-6.3.5-2.6){.pilcrow}
:   

Tf:
:   A time, the end of a measurement interval (format \"date‑time\" as
    specified in [Section
    5.6](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc3339#section-5.6){.relref} of
    \[[RFC3339](#RFC3339){.xref}\]; see also \"date‑and‑time\" in
    [Section
    3](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6991#section-3){.relref} of
    \[[RFC6991](#RFC6991){.xref}\]). The UTC Time Zone is required by
    [Section
    6.1](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc2330#section-6.1){.relref} of
    \[[RFC2330](#RFC2330){.xref}\]. When T0 is \"all-zeros\", an ending
    time and date is ignored and Tf is interpreted as the duration of
    the measurement interval.[¶](#section-6.3.5-2.8){.pilcrow}
:   

Reciprocal_lambda:
:   Average packet interval for Poisson streams, expressed in units of
    seconds, as a positive value of type decimal64 with fraction digits
    = 4 (see [Section
    9.3](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6020#section-9.3){.relref} of
    \[[RFC6020](#RFC6020){.xref}\]) with a resolution of 0.0001 seconds
    (0.1 ms), and with lossless conversion to/from the 32-bit NTP
    timestamp as per [Section
    6](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc5905#section-6){.relref} of
    \[[RFC5905](#RFC5905){.xref}\].[¶](#section-6.3.5-2.10){.pilcrow}
:   

Trunc:
:   Upper limit on Poisson distribution, expressed in units of seconds,
    as a positive value of type decimal64 with fraction digits = 4 (see
    [Section
    9.3](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6020#section-9.3){.relref} of
    \[[RFC6020](#RFC6020){.xref}\]) with a resolution of 0.0001 seconds
    (0.1 ms), and with lossless conversion to/from the 32-bit NTP
    timestamp as per [Section
    6](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc5905#section-6){.relref} of
    \[[RFC5905](#RFC5905){.xref}\] (values above this limit will be
    clipped and set to the limit
    value).[¶](#section-6.3.5-2.12){.pilcrow}
:   

ID:
:   The 16-bit Identifier assigned by the program that generates the
    query. The ID value must vary in successive queries (a list of IDs
    is needed); see [Section
    4.1.1](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc1035#section-4.1.1){.relref}
    of \[[RFC1035](#RFC1035){.xref}\]. This Identifier is copied into
    the corresponding reply and can be used by the requester (Src) to
    match replies with any outstanding
    queries.[¶](#section-6.3.5-2.14){.pilcrow}
:   

QNAME:
:   The domain name of the query, formatted as specified in [Section
    4](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6991#section-4){.relref} of
    \[[RFC6991](#RFC6991){.xref}\].[¶](#section-6.3.5-2.16){.pilcrow}
:   

QTYPE:
:   The query type, which will correspond to the IP address family of
    the query (decimal 1 for IPv4 or 28 for IPv6), formatted as a
    uint16, as per [Section
    9.2](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6020#section-9.2){.relref} of
    \[[RFC6020](#RFC6020){.xref}\].[¶](#section-6.3.5-2.18){.pilcrow}
:   
:::

::: {#section-6.3.6 .section}
#### [6.3.6.](#section-6.3.6){.section-number .selfRef} [Roles](#name-roles-3){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-roles-3}

[]{.break}

Src:
:   Launches each packet and waits for return transmissions from the
    Dst.[¶](#section-6.3.6-1.2){.pilcrow}
:   

Dst:
:   Waits for each packet from the Src and sends a return packet to the
    Src.[¶](#section-6.3.6-1.4){.pilcrow}
:   
:::
:::

::: {#section-6.4 .section}
### [6.4.](#section-6.4){.section-number .selfRef} [Output](#name-output-3){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-output-3}

This category specifies all details of the output of measurements using
the metric.[¶](#section-6.4-1){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-6.4.1 .section}
#### [6.4.1.](#section-6.4.1){.section-number .selfRef} [Type](#name-type-3){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-type-3}

Raw: For each DNS query packet sent, sets of values as defined in the
next column, including the status of the response, only assigning delay
values to successful query-response
pairs.[¶](#section-6.4.1-1){.pilcrow}
:::

::: {#section-6.4.2 .section}
#### [6.4.2.](#section-6.4.2){.section-number .selfRef} [Reference Definition](#name-reference-definition-6){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-reference-definition-6}

For all outputs:[¶](#section-6.4.2-1){.pilcrow}

[]{.break}

T:
:   The time the DNS query was sent during the measurement interval
    (format \"date‑time\" as specified in [Section
    5.6](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc3339#section-5.6){.relref} of
    \[[RFC3339](#RFC3339){.xref}\]; see also \"date‑and‑time\" in
    [Section
    3](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6991#section-3){.relref} of
    \[[RFC6991](#RFC6991){.xref}\]). The UTC Time Zone is required by
    [Section
    6.1](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc2330#section-6.1){.relref} of
    \[[RFC2330](#RFC2330){.xref}\].[¶](#section-6.4.2-2.2){.pilcrow}
:   

dT:
:   The time value of the round-trip delay to receive the DNS Response,
    expressed in units of seconds, as a positive value of type decimal64
    with fraction digits = 9 (see [Section
    9.3](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6020#section-9.3){.relref} of
    \[[RFC6020](#RFC6020){.xref}\]) with a resolution of 0.000000001
    seconds (1.0 ns), and with lossless conversion to/from the 64-bit
    NTP timestamp as per [Section
    6](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc5905#section-6){.relref} of
    \[[RFC5905](#RFC5905){.xref}\]. This value is undefined when the
    response packet is not received at the Src within a waiting time of
    Tmax seconds.[¶](#section-6.4.2-2.4){.pilcrow}
:   

RCODE:
:   The value of the RCODE field in the DNS Response header, expressed
    as a uint64 as specified in [Section
    9.2](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6020#section-9.2){.relref} of
    \[[RFC6020](#RFC6020){.xref}\]. Non-zero values convey errors in the
    response, and such replies must be analyzed separately from
    successful requests.[¶](#section-6.4.2-2.6){.pilcrow}
:   

Logical:
:   The numeric value of the result is expressed as a Logical value,
    where 1 = Lost and 0 = Received, as a positive value of type uint8
    (represents integer values between 0 and 255, inclusively (see
    [Section
    9.2](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6020#section-9.2){.relref} of
    \[[RFC6020](#RFC6020){.xref}\]). Note that for queries with outcome
    1 = Lost, dT and RCODE will be set to the maximum for decimal64 and
    uint64, respectively.[¶](#section-6.4.2-2.8){.pilcrow}
:   
:::

::: {#section-6.4.3 .section}
#### [6.4.3.](#section-6.4.3){.section-number .selfRef} [Metric Units](#name-metric-units-3){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-metric-units-3}

[]{.break}

RTDNS:
:   Round-trip delay, dT, is expressed in
    seconds.[¶](#section-6.4.3-1.2){.pilcrow}
:   

RLDNS:
:   The Logical value, where 1 = Lost and 0 =
    Received.[¶](#section-6.4.3-1.4){.pilcrow}
:   
:::

::: {#section-6.4.4 .section}
#### [6.4.4.](#section-6.4.4){.section-number .selfRef} [Calibration](#name-calibration-3){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-calibration-3}

[Section
3.7.3](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc7679#section-3.7.3){.relref} of
\[[RFC7679](#RFC7679){.xref}\] provides a means to quantify the
systematic and random errors of a time measurement. Calibration in-situ
could be enabled with an internal loopback at the Source host that
includes as much of the measurement system as possible, performs address
and payload manipulation as needed, and provides some form of isolation
(e.g., deterministic delay) to avoid send-receive interface contention.
Some portion of the random and systematic error can be characterized in
this way.[¶](#section-6.4.4-1){.pilcrow}

When a measurement controller requests a calibration measurement, the
loopback is applied and the result is output in the same format as a
normal measurement, with an additional indication that it is a
calibration result.[¶](#section-6.4.4-2){.pilcrow}

Both internal loopback calibration and clock synchronization can be used
to estimate the available accuracy of the Output Metric Units. For
example, repeated loopback delay measurements will reveal the portion of
the output result resolution that is the result of system noise and is
thus inaccurate.[¶](#section-6.4.4-3){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#section-7 .section}
## [7.](#section-7){.section-number .selfRef} [UDP Poisson One-Way Delay and Loss Registry Entries](#name-udp-poisson-one-way-delay-a){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-udp-poisson-one-way-delay-a}

This section specifies five initial Registry Entries for UDP Poisson
One-Way Delay and one entry for UDP Poisson One-Way
Loss.[¶](#section-7-1){.pilcrow}

All column entries besides the ID, Name, Description, and Output
Reference Method categories are the same; thus, this section defines six
closely related Registry Entries. As a result, IANA has assigned
corresponding URLs to each of the Named
Metrics.[¶](#section-7-2){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-7.1 .section}
### [7.1.](#section-7.1){.section-number .selfRef} [Summary](#name-summary-4){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-summary-4}

This category includes multiple indexes to the Registry Entries: the
element ID and Metric Name.[¶](#section-7.1-1){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-7.1.1 .section}
#### [7.1.1.](#section-7.1.1){.section-number .selfRef} [ID (Identifier)](#name-id-identifier-4){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-id-identifier-4}

IANA has allocated the numeric Identifiers 6-11 for the six Named Metric
Entries in [Section 7](#udp-poisson-owd-owl-reg){.xref}. See [Section
7.1.2](#name712){.xref} for mapping to
Names.[¶](#section-7.1.1-1){.pilcrow}
:::

::: {#name712}
::: {#section-7.1.2 .section}
#### [7.1.2.](#section-7.1.2){.section-number .selfRef} [Name](#name-name-4){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-name-4}

[]{.break}

6:
:   OWDelay_Active_IP-UDP-Poisson-Payload250B_RFC8912sec7_Seconds_95Percentile[¶](#section-7.1.2-1.2){.pilcrow}
:   

7:
:   OWDelay_Active_IP-UDP-Poisson-Payload250B_RFC8912sec7_Seconds_Mean[¶](#section-7.1.2-1.4){.pilcrow}
:   

8:
:   OWDelay_Active_IP-UDP-Poisson-Payload250B_RFC8912sec7_Seconds_Min[¶](#section-7.1.2-1.6){.pilcrow}
:   

9:
:   OWDelay_Active_IP-UDP-Poisson-Payload250B_RFC8912sec7_Seconds_Max[¶](#section-7.1.2-1.8){.pilcrow}
:   

10:
:   OWDelay_Active_IP-UDP-Poisson-Payload250B_RFC8912sec7_Seconds_StdDev[¶](#section-7.1.2-1.10){.pilcrow}
:   

11:
:   OWLoss_Active_IP-UDP-Poisson-Payload250B_RFC8912sec7_Percent_LossRatio[¶](#section-7.1.2-1.12){.pilcrow}
:   
:::
:::

::: {#section-7.1.3 .section}
#### [7.1.3.](#section-7.1.3){.section-number .selfRef} [URI](#name-uri-4){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-uri-4}

URL:
<https://www.iana.org/assignments/performance-metrics/OWDelay_Active_IP-UDP-Poisson-Payload250B_RFC8912sec7_Seconds_95Percentile>[¶](#section-7.1.3-1){.pilcrow}

URL:
<https://www.iana.org/assignments/performance-metrics/OWDelay_Active_IP-UDP-Poisson-Payload250B_RFC8912sec7_Seconds_Mean>[¶](#section-7.1.3-2){.pilcrow}

URL:
<https://www.iana.org/assignments/performance-metrics/OWDelay_Active_IP-UDP-Poisson-Payload250B_RFC8912sec7_Seconds_Min>[¶](#section-7.1.3-3){.pilcrow}

URL:
<https://www.iana.org/assignments/performance-metrics/OWDelay_Active_IP-UDP-Poisson-Payload250B_RFC8912sec7_Seconds_Max>[¶](#section-7.1.3-4){.pilcrow}

URL:
<https://www.iana.org/assignments/performance-metrics/OWDelay_Active_IP-UDP-Poisson-Payload250B_RFC8912sec7_Seconds_StdDev>[¶](#section-7.1.3-5){.pilcrow}

URL:
<https://www.iana.org/assignments/performance-metrics/OWLoss_Active_IP-UDP-Poisson-Payload250B_RFC8912sec7_Percent_LossRatio>[¶](#section-7.1.3-6){.pilcrow}
:::

::: {#section-7.1.4 .section}
#### [7.1.4.](#section-7.1.4){.section-number .selfRef} [Description](#name-description-4){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-description-4}

[]{.break}

OWDelay:

:   This metric assesses the delay of a stream of packets exchanged
    between two hosts (or measurement points) and reports the
    \<statistic> of one-way delay for all successfully exchanged packets
    based on their conditional delay
    distribution.[¶](#section-7.1.4-1.2.1){.pilcrow}

    where \<statistic> is one of:[¶](#section-7.1.4-1.2.2){.pilcrow}

    -   [95Percentile[¶](#section-7.1.4-1.2.3.1){.pilcrow}]{#section-7.1.4-1.2.3.1}
    -   [Mean[¶](#section-7.1.4-1.2.3.2){.pilcrow}]{#section-7.1.4-1.2.3.2}
    -   [Min[¶](#section-7.1.4-1.2.3.3){.pilcrow}]{#section-7.1.4-1.2.3.3}
    -   [Max[¶](#section-7.1.4-1.2.3.4){.pilcrow}]{#section-7.1.4-1.2.3.4}
    -   [StdDev[¶](#section-7.1.4-1.2.3.5){.pilcrow}]{#section-7.1.4-1.2.3.5}

:   

OWLoss:
:   This metric assesses the loss ratio of a stream of packets exchanged
    between two hosts (which are the two measurement points). The output
    is the one-way loss ratio for all transmitted packets expressed as a
    percentage.[¶](#section-7.1.4-1.4){.pilcrow}
:   
:::

::: {#section-7.1.5 .section}
#### [7.1.5.](#section-7.1.5){.section-number .selfRef} [Change Controller](#name-change-controller-4){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-change-controller-4}

IETF[¶](#section-7.1.5-1){.pilcrow}
:::

::: {#section-7.1.6 .section}

1.0[¶](#section-7.1.6-1){.pilcrow}
:::

::: {#section-7.2 .section}
### [7.2.](#section-7.2){.section-number .selfRef} [Metric Definition](#name-metric-definition-4){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-metric-definition-4}

This category includes columns to prompt the entry of all necessary
details related to the metric definition, including the RFC reference
and values of input factors, called \"Fixed
Parameters\".[¶](#section-7.2-1){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-7.2.1 .section}
#### [7.2.1.](#section-7.2.1){.section-number .selfRef} [Reference Definition](#name-reference-definition-7){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-reference-definition-7}

For delay:[¶](#section-7.2.1-1){.pilcrow}

Almes, G., Kalidindi, S., Zekauskas, M., and A. Morton, Ed., \"A One-Way
Delay Metric for IP Performance Metrics (IPPM)\", STD 81, RFC 7679, DOI
10.17487/RFC7679, January 2016,
\<https://www.rfc-editor.org/info/rfc7679>.
\[[RFC7679](#RFC7679){.xref}\][¶](#section-7.2.1-2){.pilcrow}

Morton, A. and E. Stephan, \"Spatial Composition of Metrics\", RFC 6049,
DOI 10.17487/RFC6049, January 2011,
\<https://www.rfc-editor.org/info/rfc6049>.
\[[RFC6049](#RFC6049){.xref}\][¶](#section-7.2.1-3){.pilcrow}

[Section
3.4](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc7679#section-3.4){.relref} of
\[[RFC7679](#RFC7679){.xref}\] provides the reference definition of the
singleton (single value) one-way delay metric. [Section
4.4](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc7679#section-4.4){.relref} of
\[[RFC7679](#RFC7679){.xref}\] provides the reference definition
expanded to cover a multi-value sample. Note that terms such as
\"singleton\" and \"sample\" are defined in [Section
11](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc2330#section-11){.relref} of
\[[RFC2330](#RFC2330){.xref}\].[¶](#section-7.2.1-4){.pilcrow}

Only successful packet transfers with finite delay are included in the
sample, as prescribed in [Section
4.1.2](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6049#section-4.1.2){.relref} of
\[[RFC6049](#RFC6049){.xref}\].[¶](#section-7.2.1-5){.pilcrow}

For loss:[¶](#section-7.2.1-6){.pilcrow}

Almes, G., Kalidindi, S., Zekauskas, M., and A. Morton, Ed., \"A One-Way
Loss Metric for IP Performance Metrics (IPPM)\", STD 82, RFC 7680, DOI
10.17487/RFC7680, January 2016,
\<https://www.rfc-editor.org/info/rfc7680>.
\[[RFC7680](#RFC7680){.xref}\][¶](#section-7.2.1-7){.pilcrow}

[Section
2.4](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc7680#section-2.4){.relref} of
\[[RFC7680](#RFC7680){.xref}\] provides the reference definition of the
singleton (single value) one-way Loss metric. [Section
3.4](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc7680#section-3.4){.relref} of
\[[RFC7680](#RFC7680){.xref}\] provides the reference definition
expanded to cover a multi-singleton sample. Note that terms such as
\"singleton\" and \"sample\" are defined in [Section
11](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc2330#section-11){.relref} of
\[[RFC2330](#RFC2330){.xref}\].[¶](#section-7.2.1-8){.pilcrow}
:::

::: {#section-7.2.2 .section}
#### [7.2.2.](#section-7.2.2){.section-number .selfRef} [Fixed Parameters](#name-fixed-parameters-4){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-fixed-parameters-4}

[]{.break}

Type-P:
:   []{.break}

    IPv4 header values:
    :   []{.break}

        DSCP:
        :   Set to 0[¶](#section-7.2.2-1.2.2.2.2.2){.pilcrow}
        :   

        TTL:
        :   Set to 255[¶](#section-7.2.2-1.2.2.2.2.4){.pilcrow}
        :   

        Protocol:
        :   Set to 17 (UDP)[¶](#section-7.2.2-1.2.2.2.2.6){.pilcrow}
        :   
    :   

    []{.break}

    IPv6 header values:
    :   []{.break}

        DSCP:
        :   Set to 0[¶](#section-7.2.2-1.2.3.2.2.2){.pilcrow}
        :   

        Hop Count:
        :   Set to 255[¶](#section-7.2.2-1.2.3.2.2.4){.pilcrow}
        :   

        Next Header:
        :   Set to 17 (UDP)[¶](#section-7.2.2-1.2.3.2.2.6){.pilcrow}
        :   

        Flow Label:
        :   Set to 0[¶](#section-7.2.2-1.2.3.2.2.8){.pilcrow}
        :   

        Extension Headers:
        :   None[¶](#section-7.2.2-1.2.3.2.2.10){.pilcrow}
        :   
    :   

    []{.break}

    UDP header values:
    :   []{.break}

        Checksum:
        :   The checksum [MUST]{.bcp14} be calculated and the non-zero
            checksum included in the
            header[¶](#section-7.2.2-1.2.4.2.2.2){.pilcrow}
        :   
    :   

    []{.break}

    UDP Payload:

    :   TWAMP-Test packet formats ([Section
        4.1.2](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc5357#section-4.1.2){.relref}
        of
        \[[RFC5357](#RFC5357){.xref}\])[¶](#section-7.2.2-1.2.5.2.1){.pilcrow}

        -   [Security features in use influence the number of Padding
            octets[¶](#section-7.2.2-1.2.5.2.2.1){.pilcrow}]{#section-7.2.2-1.2.5.2.2.1}
        -   [250 octets total, including the TWAMP format type, which
            [MUST]{.bcp14} be
            reported[¶](#section-7.2.2-1.2.5.2.2.2){.pilcrow}]{#section-7.2.2-1.2.5.2.2.2}

    :   
:   

[]{.break}

Other measurement Parameters:
:   []{.break}

    Tmax:
    :   A loss threshold waiting time with value 3.0, expressed in units
        of seconds, as a positive value of type decimal64 with fraction
        digits = 4 (see [Section
        9.3](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6020#section-9.3){.relref}
        of \[[RFC6020](#RFC6020){.xref}\]) and with a resolution of
        0.0001 seconds (0.1 ms), with lossless conversion to/from the
        32-bit NTP timestamp as per [Section
        6](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc5905#section-6){.relref} of
        \[[RFC5905](#RFC5905){.xref}\].[¶](#section-7.2.2-2.2.2.2){.pilcrow}
    :   
:   

See the Packet Stream Generation section for two additional Fixed
Parameters.[¶](#section-7.2.2-3){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#section-7.3 .section}
### [7.3.](#section-7.3){.section-number .selfRef} [Method of Measurement](#name-method-of-measurement-4){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-method-of-measurement-4}

This category includes columns for references to relevant sections of
the RFC(s) and any supplemental information needed to ensure an
unambiguous method for implementations.[¶](#section-7.3-1){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-7.3.1 .section}
#### [7.3.1.](#section-7.3.1){.section-number .selfRef} [Reference Methods](#name-reference-methods-4){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-reference-methods-4}

The methodology for this metric (equivalent to
Type-P-One-way-Delay-Poisson-Stream) is defined as in [Section
3.6](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc7679#section-3.6){.relref} of
\[[RFC7679](#RFC7679){.xref}\] (for singletons) and [Section
4.6](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc7679#section-4.6){.relref} of
\[[RFC7679](#RFC7679){.xref}\] (for samples) using the Type-P and Tmax
defined in the Fixed Parameters column.[¶](#section-7.3.1-1){.pilcrow}

The reference method distinguishes between long-delayed packets and lost
packets by implementing a maximum waiting time for packet arrival. Tmax
is the waiting time used as the threshold to declare a packet lost. Lost
packets [SHALL]{.bcp14} be designated as having undefined delay and
counted for the OWLoss metric.[¶](#section-7.3.1-2){.pilcrow}

The calculations on the one-way delay [SHALL]{.bcp14} be performed on
the conditional distribution, conditioned on successful packet arrival
within Tmax. Also, when all packet delays are stored, the process that
calculates the one-way delay value [MUST]{.bcp14} enforce the Tmax
threshold on stored values before calculations. See [Section
4.1](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc3393#section-4.1){.relref} of
\[[RFC3393](#RFC3393){.xref}\] for details on the conditional
distribution to exclude undefined values of delay, and see [Section
5](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6703#section-5){.relref} of
\[[RFC6703](#RFC6703){.xref}\] for background on this analysis
choice.[¶](#section-7.3.1-3){.pilcrow}

The reference method requires some way to distinguish between different
packets in a stream to establish correspondence between sending times
and receiving times for each successfully arriving
packet.[¶](#section-7.3.1-4){.pilcrow}

Since a standard measurement protocol is employed
\[[RFC5357](#RFC5357){.xref}\], the measurement process will determine
the sequence numbers or timestamps applied to test packets after the
Fixed and Runtime Parameters are passed to that process. The measurement
protocol dictates the format of sequence numbers and timestamps conveyed
in the TWAMP-Test packet payload.[¶](#section-7.3.1-5){.pilcrow}
:::

::: {#section-7.3.2 .section}
#### [7.3.2.](#section-7.3.2){.section-number .selfRef} [Packet Stream Generation](#name-packet-stream-generation-4){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-packet-stream-generation-4}

This section provides details regarding packet traffic, which is used as
the basis for measurement. In IPPM Metrics, this is called the
\"stream\"; this stream can easily be described by providing the list of
stream Parameters.[¶](#section-7.3.2-1){.pilcrow}

[Section
11.1.3](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc2330#section-11.1.3){.relref}
of \[[RFC2330](#RFC2330){.xref}\] provides three methods to generate
Poisson sampling intervals. The reciprocal of lambda is the average
packet spacing; thus, the Runtime Parameter is
Reciprocal_lambda = 1⁠/lambda, in
seconds.[¶](#section-7.3.2-2){.pilcrow}

Method 3 [SHALL]{.bcp14} be used. Where given a start time (Runtime
Parameter), the subsequent send times are all computed prior to
measurement by computing the pseudorandom distribution of inter-packet
send times (truncating the distribution as specified in the Parameter
Trunc), and the Src sends each packet at the computed
times.[¶](#section-7.3.2-3){.pilcrow}

Note that Trunc is the upper limit on inter-packet times in the Poisson
distribution. A random value greater than Trunc is set equal to Trunc
instead.[¶](#section-7.3.2-4){.pilcrow}

[]{.break}

Reciprocal_lambda:
:   Average packet interval for Poisson streams, expressed in units of
    seconds, as a positive value of type decimal64 with fraction digits
    = 4 (see [Section
    9.3](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6020#section-9.3){.relref} of
    \[[RFC6020](#RFC6020){.xref}\]) with a resolution of 0.0001 seconds
    (0.1 ms), and with lossless conversion to/from the 32-bit NTP
    timestamp as per [Section
    6](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc5905#section-6){.relref} of
    \[[RFC5905](#RFC5905){.xref}\]. Reciprocal_lambda = 1
    second.[¶](#section-7.3.2-5.2){.pilcrow}
:   

Trunc:
:   Upper limit on Poisson distribution, expressed in units of seconds,
    as a positive value of type decimal64 with fraction digits = 4 (see
    [Section
    9.3](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6020#section-9.3){.relref} of
    \[[RFC6020](#RFC6020){.xref}\]) with a resolution of 0.0001 seconds
    (0.1 ms), and with lossless conversion to/from the 32-bit NTP
    timestamp as per [Section
    6](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc5905#section-6){.relref} of
    \[[RFC5905](#RFC5905){.xref}\] (values above this limit will be
    clipped and set to the limit value). Trunc = 30.0000
    seconds.[¶](#section-7.3.2-5.4){.pilcrow}
:   
:::

::: {#section-7.3.3 .section}
#### [7.3.3.](#section-7.3.3){.section-number .selfRef} [Traffic Filtering (Observation) Details](#name-traffic-filtering-observation-){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-traffic-filtering-observation-}

N/A[¶](#section-7.3.3-1){.pilcrow}
:::

::: {#section-7.3.4 .section}
#### [7.3.4.](#section-7.3.4){.section-number .selfRef} [Sampling Distribution](#name-sampling-distribution-4){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-sampling-distribution-4}

N/A[¶](#section-7.3.4-1){.pilcrow}
:::

::: {#section-7.3.5 .section}
#### [7.3.5.](#section-7.3.5){.section-number .selfRef} [Runtime Parameters and Data Format](#name-runtime-parameters-and-data-fo){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-runtime-parameters-and-data-fo}

Runtime Parameters are input factors that must be determined, configured
into the measurement system, and reported with the results for the
context to be complete.[¶](#section-7.3.5-1){.pilcrow}

[]{.break}

Src:
:   The IP address of the host in the Src Role (format
    ipv4‑address-no-zone value for IPv4 or ipv6-address-no-zone value
    for IPv6; see [Section
    4](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6991#section-4){.relref} of
    \[[RFC6991](#RFC6991){.xref}\]).[¶](#section-7.3.5-2.2){.pilcrow}
:   

Dst:
:   The IP address of the host in the Dst Role (format
    ipv4‑address-no-zone value for IPv4 or ipv6-address-no-zone value
    for IPv6; see [Section
    4](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6991#section-4){.relref} of
    \[[RFC6991](#RFC6991){.xref}\]).[¶](#section-7.3.5-2.4){.pilcrow}
:   

T0:
:   A time, the start of a measurement interval (format \"date‑time\" as
    specified in [Section
    5.6](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc3339#section-5.6){.relref} of
    \[[RFC3339](#RFC3339){.xref}\]; see also \"date‑and‑time\" in
    [Section
    3](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6991#section-3){.relref} of
    \[[RFC6991](#RFC6991){.xref}\]). The UTC Time Zone is required by
    [Section
    6.1](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc2330#section-6.1){.relref} of
    \[[RFC2330](#RFC2330){.xref}\]. When T0 is \"all-zeros\", a start
    time is unspecified and Tf is to be interpreted as the duration of
    the measurement interval. The start time is controlled through other
    means.[¶](#section-7.3.5-2.6){.pilcrow}
:   

Tf:
:   A time, the end of a measurement interval (format \"date‑time\" as
    specified in [Section
    5.6](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc3339#section-5.6){.relref} of
    \[[RFC3339](#RFC3339){.xref}\]; see also \"date‑and‑time\" in
    [Section
    3](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6991#section-3){.relref} of
    \[[RFC6991](#RFC6991){.xref}\]). The UTC Time Zone is required by
    [Section
    6.1](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc2330#section-6.1){.relref} of
    \[[RFC2330](#RFC2330){.xref}\]. When T0 is \"all-zeros\", an ending
    time and date is ignored and Tf is interpreted as the duration of
    the measurement interval.[¶](#section-7.3.5-2.8){.pilcrow}
:   
:::

::: {#section-7.3.6 .section}
#### [7.3.6.](#section-7.3.6){.section-number .selfRef} [Roles](#name-roles-4){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-roles-4}

[]{.break}

Src:
:   Launches each packet and waits for return transmissions from the
    Dst.  An example is the TWAMP
    Session-Sender.[¶](#section-7.3.6-1.2){.pilcrow}
:   

Dst:
:   Waits for each packet from the Src and sends a return packet to the
    Src.  An example is the TWAMP
    Session-Reflector.[¶](#section-7.3.6-1.4){.pilcrow}
:   
:::
:::

::: {#section-7.4 .section}
### [7.4.](#section-7.4){.section-number .selfRef} [Output](#name-output-4){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-output-4}

This category specifies all details of the output of measurements using
the metric.[¶](#section-7.4-1){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-7.4.1 .section}
#### [7.4.1.](#section-7.4.1){.section-number .selfRef} [Type](#name-type-4){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-type-4}

Types are discussed in the subsections
below.[¶](#section-7.4.1-1){.pilcrow}
:::

::: {#section-7.4.2 .section}
#### [7.4.2.](#section-7.4.2){.section-number .selfRef} [Reference Definition](#name-reference-definition-8){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-reference-definition-8}

For all output types:[¶](#section-7.4.2-1){.pilcrow}

[]{.break}

T0:
:   The start of a measurement interval (format \"date‑time\" as
    specified in [Section
    5.6](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc3339#section-5.6){.relref} of
    \[[RFC3339](#RFC3339){.xref}\]; see also \"date‑and‑time\" in
    [Section
    3](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6991#section-3){.relref} of
    \[[RFC6991](#RFC6991){.xref}\]). The UTC Time Zone is required by
    [Section
    6.1](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc2330#section-6.1){.relref} of
    \[[RFC2330](#RFC2330){.xref}\].[¶](#section-7.4.2-2.2){.pilcrow}
:   

Tf:
:   The end of a measurement interval (format \"date‑time\" as specified
    in [Section
    5.6](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc3339#section-5.6){.relref} of
    \[[RFC3339](#RFC3339){.xref}\]; see also \"date‑and‑time\" in
    [Section
    3](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6991#section-3){.relref} of
    \[[RFC6991](#RFC6991){.xref}\]). The UTC Time Zone is required by
    [Section
    6.1](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc2330#section-6.1){.relref} of
    \[[RFC2330](#RFC2330){.xref}\].[¶](#section-7.4.2-2.4){.pilcrow}
:   

For LossRatio, the count of lost packets to total packets sent is the
basis for the loss ratio calculation as per [Section
4.1](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc7680#section-4.1){.relref} of
\[[RFC7680](#RFC7680){.xref}\].[¶](#section-7.4.2-3){.pilcrow}

For each \<statistic> or Percent_LossRatio, one of the following
subsections applies.[¶](#section-7.4.2-4){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-7.4.2.1 .section}
##### [7.4.2.1.](#section-7.4.2.1){.section-number .selfRef} [Percentile95](#name-percentile95){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-percentile95}

The 95th percentile [SHALL]{.bcp14} be calculated using the conditional
distribution of all packets with a finite value of one-way delay
(undefined delays are excluded) \-- a single value, as
follows:[¶](#section-7.4.2.1-1){.pilcrow}

See [Section
4.1](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc3393#section-4.1){.relref} of
\[[RFC3393](#RFC3393){.xref}\] for details on the conditional
distribution to exclude undefined values of delay, and see [Section
5](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6703#section-5){.relref} of
\[[RFC6703](#RFC6703){.xref}\] for background on this analysis
choice.[¶](#section-7.4.2.1-2){.pilcrow}

See [Section
4.3](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc3393#section-4.3){.relref} of
\[[RFC3393](#RFC3393){.xref}\] for details on the percentile statistic
(where round-trip delay should be substituted for
\"ipdv\").[¶](#section-7.4.2.1-3){.pilcrow}

The percentile = 95, meaning that the reported delay, \"95Percentile\",
is the smallest value of one-way delay for which the Empirical
Distribution Function, EDF(95Percentile), is greater than or equal to
95% of the singleton one-way delay values in the conditional
distribution. See [Section
11.3](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc2330#section-11.3){.relref} of
\[[RFC2330](#RFC2330){.xref}\] for the definition of the percentile
statistic using the EDF.[¶](#section-7.4.2.1-4){.pilcrow}

[]{.break}

95Percentile:
:   The time value of the result is expressed in units of seconds, as a
    positive value of type decimal64 with fraction digits = 9 (see
    [Section
    9.3](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6020#section-9.3){.relref} of
    \[[RFC6020](#RFC6020){.xref}\]) with a resolution of 0.000000001
    seconds (1.0 ns), and with lossless conversion to/from the 64-bit
    NTP timestamp as per [Section
    6](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc5905#section-6){.relref} of
    \[[RFC5905](#RFC5905){.xref}\].[¶](#section-7.4.2.1-5.2){.pilcrow}
:   
:::

::: {#mean-sec7422}
::: {#section-7.4.2.2 .section}
##### [7.4.2.2.](#section-7.4.2.2){.section-number .selfRef} [Mean](#name-mean){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-mean}

The mean [SHALL]{.bcp14} be calculated using the conditional
distribution of all packets with a finite value of one-way delay
(undefined delays are excluded) \-- a single value, as
follows:[¶](#section-7.4.2.2-1){.pilcrow}

See [Section
4.1](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc3393#section-4.1){.relref} of
\[[RFC3393](#RFC3393){.xref}\] for details on the conditional
distribution to exclude undefined values of delay, and see [Section
5](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6703#section-5){.relref} of
\[[RFC6703](#RFC6703){.xref}\] for background on this analysis
choice.[¶](#section-7.4.2.2-2){.pilcrow}

See [Section
4.2.2](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6049#section-4.2.2){.relref} of
\[[RFC6049](#RFC6049){.xref}\] for details on calculating this
statistic; see also [Section
4.2.3](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6049#section-4.2.3){.relref} of
\[[RFC6049](#RFC6049){.xref}\].[¶](#section-7.4.2.2-3){.pilcrow}

[]{.break}

Mean:
:   The time value of the result is expressed in units of seconds, as a
    positive value of type decimal64 with fraction digits = 9 (see
    [Section
    9.3](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6020#section-9.3){.relref} of
    \[[RFC6020](#RFC6020){.xref}\]) with a resolution of
    0.000000001 seconds (1.0 ns), and with lossless conversion to/from
    the 64-bit NTP timestamp as per [Section
    6](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc5905#section-6){.relref} of
    \[[RFC5905](#RFC5905){.xref}\].[¶](#section-7.4.2.2-4.2){.pilcrow}
:   
:::
:::

::: {#section-7.4.2.3 .section}
##### [7.4.2.3.](#section-7.4.2.3){.section-number .selfRef} [Min](#name-min){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-min}

The minimum [SHALL]{.bcp14} be calculated using the conditional
distribution of all packets with a finite value of one-way delay
(undefined delays are excluded) \-- a single value, as
follows:[¶](#section-7.4.2.3-1){.pilcrow}

See [Section
4.1](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc3393#section-4.1){.relref} of
\[[RFC3393](#RFC3393){.xref}\] for details on the conditional
distribution to exclude undefined values of delay, and see [Section
5](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6703#section-5){.relref} of
\[[RFC6703](#RFC6703){.xref}\] for background on this analysis
choice.[¶](#section-7.4.2.3-2){.pilcrow}

See [Section
4.3.2](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6049#section-4.3.2){.relref} of
\[[RFC6049](#RFC6049){.xref}\] for details on calculating this
statistic; see also [Section
4.3.3](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6049#section-4.3.3){.relref} of
\[[RFC6049](#RFC6049){.xref}\].[¶](#section-7.4.2.3-3){.pilcrow}

[]{.break}

Min:
:   The time value of the result is expressed in units of seconds, as a
    positive value of type decimal64 with fraction digits = 9 (see
    [Section
    9.3](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6020#section-9.3){.relref} of
    \[[RFC6020](#RFC6020){.xref}\]) with a resolution of
    0.000000001 seconds (1.0 ns), and with lossless conversion to/from
    the 64-bit NTP timestamp as per [Section
    6](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc5905#section-6){.relref} of
    \[[RFC5905](#RFC5905){.xref}\].[¶](#section-7.4.2.3-4.2){.pilcrow}
:   
:::

::: {#section-7.4.2.4 .section}
##### [7.4.2.4.](#section-7.4.2.4){.section-number .selfRef} [Max](#name-max){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-max}

The maximum [SHALL]{.bcp14} be calculated using the conditional
distribution of all packets with a finite value of one-way delay
(undefined delays are excluded) \-- a single value, as
follows:[¶](#section-7.4.2.4-1){.pilcrow}

See [Section
4.1](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc3393#section-4.1){.relref} of
\[[RFC3393](#RFC3393){.xref}\] for details on the conditional
distribution to exclude undefined values of delay, and see [Section
5](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6703#section-5){.relref} of
\[[RFC6703](#RFC6703){.xref}\] for background on this analysis
choice.[¶](#section-7.4.2.4-2){.pilcrow}

See [Section
4.3.2](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6049#section-4.3.2){.relref} of
\[[RFC6049](#RFC6049){.xref}\] for a closely related method for
calculating this statistic; see also [Section
4.3.3](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6049#section-4.3.3){.relref} of
\[[RFC6049](#RFC6049){.xref}\]. The formula is as
follows:[¶](#section-7.4.2.4-3){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-7.4.2.4-4 .alignLeft .art-text .artwork}
       Max = (FiniteDelay[j])

[¶](#section-7.4.2.4-4){.pilcrow}
:::

-   [such that for some index, j, where 1 \<= j \<= N
    FiniteDelay\[j\] >= FiniteDelay\[n\] for all
    n[¶](#section-7.4.2.4-5.1){.pilcrow}]{#section-7.4.2.4-5.1}

[]{.break}

Max:
:   The time value of the result is expressed in units of seconds, as a
    positive value of type decimal64 with fraction digits = 9 (see
    [Section
    9.3](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6020#section-9.3){.relref} of
    \[[RFC6020](#RFC6020){.xref}\]) with a resolution of
    0.000000001 seconds (1.0 ns), and with lossless conversion to/from
    the 64-bit NTP timestamp as per [Section
    6](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc5905#section-6){.relref} of
    \[[RFC5905](#RFC5905){.xref}\].[¶](#section-7.4.2.4-6.2){.pilcrow}
:   
:::

::: {#section-7.4.2.5 .section}
##### [7.4.2.5.](#section-7.4.2.5){.section-number .selfRef} [Std_Dev](#name-std_dev){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-std_dev}

The standard deviation (Std_Dev) [SHALL]{.bcp14} be calculated using the
conditional distribution of all packets with a finite value of one‑way
delay (undefined delays are excluded) \-- a single value, as
follows:[¶](#section-7.4.2.5-1){.pilcrow}

See [Section
4.1](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc3393#section-4.1){.relref} of
\[[RFC3393](#RFC3393){.xref}\] for details on the conditional
distribution to exclude undefined values of delay, and see [Section
5](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6703#section-5){.relref} of
\[[RFC6703](#RFC6703){.xref}\] for background on this analysis
choice.[¶](#section-7.4.2.5-2){.pilcrow}

See [Section
6.1.4](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6049#section-6.1.4){.relref} of
\[[RFC6049](#RFC6049){.xref}\] for a closely related method for
calculating this statistic. The formula is the classic calculation for
the standard deviation of a population.[¶](#section-7.4.2.5-3){.pilcrow}

Define Population Std_Dev_Delay as
follows:[¶](#section-7.4.2.5-4){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-7.4.2.5-5 .alignLeft .art-text .artwork}
                         _                                       _
                        |            N                            |
                        |           ---                           |
                        |     1     \                          2  |
        Std_Dev = SQRT  |  -------   >   (Delay[n] - MeanDelay)   |
                        |    (N)    /                             |
                        |           ---                           |
                        |          n = 1                          |
                        |_                                       _|

[¶](#section-7.4.2.5-5){.pilcrow}
:::

where all packets n = 1 through N have a value for Delay\[n\], MeanDelay
is calculated per [Section 7.4.2.2](#mean-sec7422){.xref}, and SQRT\[\]
is the Square Root function:[¶](#section-7.4.2.5-6){.pilcrow}

[]{.break}

Std_Dev:
:   The time value of the result is expressed in units of seconds, as a
    positive value of type decimal64 with fraction digits = 9 (see
    [Section
    9.3](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6020#section-9.3){.relref} of
    \[[RFC6020](#RFC6020){.xref}\]) with a resolution of 0.000000001
    seconds (1.0 ns), and with lossless conversion to/from the 64-bit
    NTP timestamp as per [Section
    6](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc5905#section-6){.relref} of
    \[[RFC5905](#RFC5905){.xref}\].[¶](#section-7.4.2.5-7.2){.pilcrow}
:   
:::

::: {#section-7.4.2.6 .section}
##### [7.4.2.6.](#section-7.4.2.6){.section-number .selfRef} [Percent_LossRatio](#name-percent_lossratio){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-percent_lossratio}

[]{.break}

Percent_LossRatio:
:   The numeric value of the result is expressed in units of lost
    packets to total packets times 100%, as a positive value of type
    decimal64 with fraction digits = 9 (see [Section
    9.3](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6020#section-9.3){.relref} of
    \[[RFC6020](#RFC6020){.xref}\]) with a resolution of
    0.0000000001.[¶](#section-7.4.2.6-1.2){.pilcrow}
:   
:::
:::

::: {#section-7.4.3 .section}
#### [7.4.3.](#section-7.4.3){.section-number .selfRef} [Metric Units](#name-metric-units-4){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-metric-units-4}

The \<statistic> of one-way delay is expressed in seconds, where
\<statistic> is one of:[¶](#section-7.4.3-1){.pilcrow}

-   [95Percentile[¶](#section-7.4.3-2.1){.pilcrow}]{#section-7.4.3-2.1}
-   [Mean[¶](#section-7.4.3-2.2){.pilcrow}]{#section-7.4.3-2.2}
-   [Min[¶](#section-7.4.3-2.3){.pilcrow}]{#section-7.4.3-2.3}
-   [Max[¶](#section-7.4.3-2.4){.pilcrow}]{#section-7.4.3-2.4}
-   [StdDev[¶](#section-7.4.3-2.5){.pilcrow}]{#section-7.4.3-2.5}

The one-way loss ratio is expressed as a percentage of lost packets to
total packets sent.[¶](#section-7.4.3-3){.pilcrow}
:::

::: {#section-7.4.4 .section}
#### [7.4.4.](#section-7.4.4){.section-number .selfRef} [Calibration](#name-calibration-4){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-calibration-4}

[Section
3.7.3](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc7679#section-3.7.3){.relref} of
\[[RFC7679](#RFC7679){.xref}\] provides a means to quantify the
systematic and random errors of a time measurement. Calibration in-situ
could be enabled with an internal loopback that includes as much of the
measurement system as possible, performs address manipulation as needed,
and provides some form of isolation (e.g., deterministic delay) to avoid
send-receive interface contention. Some portion of the random and
systematic error can be characterized in this
way.[¶](#section-7.4.4-1){.pilcrow}

For one-way delay measurements, the error calibration must include an
assessment of the internal clock synchronization with its external
reference (this internal clock is supplying timestamps for measurement).
In practice, the time offsets \[[RFC5905](#RFC5905){.xref}\] of clocks
at both the Source and Destination are needed to estimate the systematic
error due to imperfect clock synchronization (the time offsets
\[[RFC5905](#RFC5905){.xref}\] are smoothed; thus, the random variation
is not usually represented in the
results).[¶](#section-7.4.4-2){.pilcrow}

[]{.break}

time_offset:
:   The time value of the result is expressed in units of seconds, as a
    signed value of type decimal64 with fraction digits = 9 (see
    [Section
    9.3](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6020#section-9.3){.relref} of
    \[[RFC6020](#RFC6020){.xref}\]) with a resolution of 0.000000001
    seconds (1.0 ns), and with lossless conversion to/from the 64-bit
    NTP timestamp as per [Section
    6](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc5905#section-6){.relref} of
    \[[RFC5905](#RFC5905){.xref}\].[¶](#section-7.4.4-3.2){.pilcrow}
:   

When a measurement controller requests a calibration measurement, the
loopback is applied and the result is output in the same format as a
normal measurement, with an additional indication that it is a
calibration result. In any measurement, the measurement function
[SHOULD]{.bcp14} report its current estimate of the time offset
\[[RFC5905](#RFC5905){.xref}\] as an indicator of the degree of
synchronization.[¶](#section-7.4.4-4){.pilcrow}

Both internal loopback calibration and clock synchronization can be used
to estimate the available accuracy of the Output Metric Units. For
example, repeated loopback delay measurements will reveal the portion of
the output result resolution that is the result of system noise and is
thus inaccurate.[¶](#section-7.4.4-5){.pilcrow}
:::
:::
