::: {#tcp-rt-delay-loss-reg-entries}
::: {#section-10 .section}
## [10.](#section-10){.section-number .selfRef} [TCP Round-Trip Delay and Loss Registry Entries](#name-tcp-round-trip-delay-and-lo){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-tcp-round-trip-delay-and-lo}

This section specifies four initial Registry Entries for the Passive
assessment of TCP Round-Trip Delay (RTD) and another entry for the TCP
Round-Trip Loss Count.[¶](#section-10-1){.pilcrow}

All column entries besides the ID, Name, Description, and Output
Reference Method categories are the same; thus, this section defines
four closely related Registry Entries. As a result, IANA has assigned
corresponding URLs to each of the four Named
Metrics.[¶](#section-10-2){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-10.1 .section}
### [10.1.](#section-10.1){.section-number .selfRef} [Summary](#name-summary-7){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-summary-7}

This category includes multiple indexes to the Registry Entries: the
element ID and Metric Name.[¶](#section-10.1-1){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-10.1.1 .section}
#### [10.1.1.](#section-10.1.1){.section-number .selfRef} [ID (Identifier)](#name-id-identifier-7){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-id-identifier-7}

IANA has allocated the numeric Identifiers 22-26 for the five Named
Metric Entries in [Section 10](#tcp-rt-delay-loss-reg-entries){.xref}.
See [Section 10.1.2](#name1012){.xref} for mapping to
Names.[¶](#section-10.1.1-1){.pilcrow}
:::

::: {#name1012}
::: {#section-10.1.2 .section}
#### [10.1.2.](#section-10.1.2){.section-number .selfRef} [Name](#name-name-7){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-name-7}

[]{.break}

22:
:   RTDelay_Passive_IP-TCP_RFC8912sec10_Seconds_Mean[¶](#section-10.1.2-1.2){.pilcrow}
:   

23:
:   RTDelay_Passive_IP-TCP_RFC8912sec10_Seconds_Min[¶](#section-10.1.2-1.4){.pilcrow}
:   

24:
:   RTDelay_Passive_IP-TCP_RFC8912sec10_Seconds_Max[¶](#section-10.1.2-1.6){.pilcrow}
:   

25:
:   RTDelay_Passive_IP-TCP-HS_RFC8912sec10_Seconds_Singleton[¶](#section-10.1.2-1.8){.pilcrow}
:   

Note that a midpoint observer only has the opportunity to compose a
single RTDelay on the TCP handshake.[¶](#section-10.1.2-2){.pilcrow}

[]{.break}

26:
:   RTLoss_Passive_IP-TCP_RFC8912sec10_Packet_Count[¶](#section-10.1.2-3.2){.pilcrow}
:   
:::
:::

::: {#section-10.1.3 .section}
#### [10.1.3.](#section-10.1.3){.section-number .selfRef} [URI](#name-uri-7){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-uri-7}

URL:
<https://www.iana.org/assignments/performance-metrics/RTDelay_Passive_IP-TCP_RFC8912sec10_Seconds_Mean>[¶](#section-10.1.3-1){.pilcrow}

URL:
<https://www.iana.org/assignments/performance-metrics/RTDelay_Passive_IP-TCP_RFC8912sec10_Seconds_Min>[¶](#section-10.1.3-2){.pilcrow}

URL:
<https://www.iana.org/assignments/performance-metrics/RTDelay_Passive_IP-TCP_RFC8912sec10_Seconds_Max>[¶](#section-10.1.3-3){.pilcrow}

URL:
<https://www.iana.org/assignments/performance-metrics/RTDelay_Passive_IP-TCP-HS_RFC8912sec10_Seconds_Singleton>[¶](#section-10.1.3-4){.pilcrow}

URL:
<https://www.iana.org/assignments/performance-metrics/RTLoss_Passive_IP-TCP_RFC8912sec10_Packet_Count>[¶](#section-10.1.3-5){.pilcrow}
:::

::: {#section-10.1.4 .section}
#### [10.1.4.](#section-10.1.4){.section-number .selfRef} [Description](#name-description-7){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-description-7}

[]{.break}

RTDelay:

:   This metric assesses the round-trip delay of TCP packets
    constituting a single connection, exchanged between two hosts. We
    consider the measurement of round-trip delay based on a single
    Observation Point (OP) \[[RFC7011](#RFC7011){.xref}\] somewhere in
    the network. The output is the round-trip delay for all successfully
    exchanged packets expressed as the \<statistic> of their conditional
    delay distribution, where \<statistic> is one
    of:[¶](#section-10.1.4-1.2.1){.pilcrow}

    -   [Mean[¶](#section-10.1.4-1.2.2.1){.pilcrow}]{#section-10.1.4-1.2.2.1}
    -   [Min[¶](#section-10.1.4-1.2.2.2){.pilcrow}]{#section-10.1.4-1.2.2.2}
    -   [Max[¶](#section-10.1.4-1.2.2.3){.pilcrow}]{#section-10.1.4-1.2.2.3}

:   

RTDelay Singleton:

:   This metric assesses the round-trip delay of TCP packets initiating
    a single connection (or 3-way handshake), exchanged between two
    hosts. We consider the measurement of round-trip delay based on a
    single Observation Point (OP) \[[RFC7011](#RFC7011){.xref}\]
    somewhere in the network. The output is the single measurement of
    Round-trip delay, or Singleton.[¶](#section-10.1.4-1.4.1){.pilcrow}

:   

RTLoss:
:   This metric assesses the estimated loss count for TCP packets
    constituting a single connection, exchanged between two hosts. We
    consider the measurement of round-trip delay based on a single OP
    \[[RFC7011](#RFC7011){.xref}\] somewhere in the network. The output
    is the estimated loss count for the measurement
    interval.[¶](#section-10.1.4-1.6){.pilcrow}
:   
:::

::: {#section-10.1.5 .section}
#### [10.1.5.](#section-10.1.5){.section-number .selfRef} [Change Controller](#name-change-controller-7){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-change-controller-7}

IETF[¶](#section-10.1.5-1){.pilcrow}
:::

::: {#section-10.1.6 .section}
#### [10.1.6.](#section-10.1.6){.section-number .selfRef} [Version (of Registry Format)](#name-version-of-registry-format-7){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-version-of-registry-format-7}

1.0[¶](#section-10.1.6-1){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#section-10.2 .section}
### [10.2.](#section-10.2){.section-number .selfRef} [Metric Definition](#name-metric-definition-7){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-metric-definition-7}

This category includes columns to prompt the entry of all necessary
details related to the metric definition, including the RFC reference
and values of input factors, called \"Fixed
Parameters\".[¶](#section-10.2-1){.pilcrow}

::: {#s10.2.1}
::: {#section-10.2.1 .section}
#### [10.2.1.](#section-10.2.1){.section-number .selfRef} [Reference Definition](#name-reference-definition-13){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-reference-definition-13}

Almes, G., Kalidindi, S., and M. Zekauskas, \"A Round-trip Delay Metric
for IPPM\", RFC 2681, DOI 10.17487/RFC2681, September 1999,
\<https://www.rfc-editor.org/info/rfc2681>.
\[[RFC2681](#RFC2681){.xref}\][¶](#section-10.2.1-1){.pilcrow}

Although there is no RFC that describes Passive Measurement of
round-trip delay, the parallel definition for Active Measurement is
provided in
\[[RFC2681](#RFC2681){.xref}\].[¶](#section-10.2.1-2){.pilcrow}

This metric definition uses the term \"wire time\" as defined in
[Section
10.2](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc2330#section-10.2){.relref} of
\[[RFC2330](#RFC2330){.xref}\], and the terms \"singleton\" and
\"sample\" as defined in [Section
11](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc2330#section-11){.relref} of
\[[RFC2330](#RFC2330){.xref}\]. ([Section
2.4](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc2681#section-2.4){.relref} of
\[[RFC2681](#RFC2681){.xref}\] provides the reference definition of the
singleton (single value) round-trip delay metric. [Section
3.4](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc2681#section-3.4){.relref} of
\[[RFC2681](#RFC2681){.xref}\] provides the reference definition
expanded to cover a multi-singleton
sample.)[¶](#section-10.2.1-3){.pilcrow}

With the OP \[[RFC7011](#RFC7011){.xref}\] typically located between the
hosts participating in the TCP connection, the round-trip delay metric
requires two individual measurements between the OP and each host, such
that the Spatial Composition \[[RFC6049](#RFC6049){.xref}\] of the
measurements yields a round-trip delay singleton (we are extending the
composition of one-way subpath delays to subpath round-trip
delay).[¶](#section-10.2.1-4){.pilcrow}

Using the direction of TCP SYN transmission to anchor the nomenclature,
host A sends the SYN, and host B replies with SYN-ACK during connection
establishment. The direction of SYN transfer is considered the Forward
direction of transmission, from A through the OP to B (the Reverse
direction is B through the OP to A).[¶](#section-10.2.1-5){.pilcrow}

Traffic Filters reduce the packet streams at the OP to a Qualified
bidirectional flow of packets.[¶](#section-10.2.1-6){.pilcrow}

In the definitions below, Corresponding Packets are transferred in
different directions and convey a common value in a TCP header field
that establishes correspondence (to the extent possible). Examples may
be found in the TCP timestamp fields.[¶](#section-10.2.1-7){.pilcrow}

For a real number, RTD_fwd, \>\> the round-trip delay in the Forward
direction from the OP to host B at time T\' is RTD_fwd \<\< it is
[REQUIRED]{.bcp14} that the OP observed a Qualified Packet to host B at
wire time T\', that host B received that packet and sent a Corresponding
Packet back to host A, and the OP observed the Corresponding Packet at
wire time T\' + RTD_fwd.[¶](#section-10.2.1-8){.pilcrow}

For a real number, RTD_rev, \>\> the round-trip delay in the Reverse
direction from the OP to host A at time T\'\' is RTD_rev \<\< it is
[REQUIRED]{.bcp14} that the OP observed a Qualified Packet to host A at
wire time T\'\', that host A received that packet and sent a
Corresponding Packet back to host B, and that the OP observed the
Corresponding Packet at wire time T\'\' +
RTD_rev.[¶](#section-10.2.1-9){.pilcrow}

Ideally, the packet sent from host B to host A in both definitions above
[SHOULD]{.bcp14} be the same packet (or, when measuring RTD_rev first,
the packet from host A to host B in both definitions should be the
same).[¶](#section-10.2.1-10){.pilcrow}

The [REQUIRED]{.bcp14} Composition Function for a singleton of
round-trip delay at time T (where T is the earliest of T\' and T\'\'
above) is:[¶](#section-10.2.1-11){.pilcrow}

RTDelay = RTD_fwd + RTD_rev[¶](#section-10.2.1-12){.pilcrow}

Note that when the OP is located at host A or host B, one of the terms
composing RTDelay will be zero or
negligible.[¶](#section-10.2.1-13){.pilcrow}

Using the abbreviation HS to refer to the TCP handshake: when the
Qualified and Corresponding Packets are a TCP-SYN and a TCP‑SYN-ACK,
RTD_fwd == RTD_HS_fwd.[¶](#section-10.2.1-14){.pilcrow}

When the Qualified and Corresponding Packets are a TCP-SYN-ACK and a
TCP-ACK, RTD_rev == RTD_HS_rev.[¶](#section-10.2.1-15){.pilcrow}

The [REQUIRED]{.bcp14} Composition Function for a singleton of
round-trip delay for the connection handshake
is:[¶](#section-10.2.1-16){.pilcrow}

RTDelay_HS = RTD_HS_fwd + RTD_HS_rev[¶](#section-10.2.1-17){.pilcrow}

The definition of round-trip loss count uses the nomenclature developed
above, based on observation of the TCP header sequence numbers and
storing the sequence number gaps observed. Packet losses can be inferred
from:[¶](#section-10.2.1-18){.pilcrow}

[]{.break}

Out-of-order segments:
:   TCP segments are transmitted with monotonically increasing sequence
    numbers, but these segments may be received out of order. [Section
    3](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc4737#section-3){.relref} of
    \[[RFC4737](#RFC4737){.xref}\] describes the notion of \"next
    expected\" sequence numbers, which can be adapted to TCP segments
    (for the purpose of detecting reordered packets). Observation of
    out-of-order segments indicates loss on the path prior to the OP and
    creates a gap.[¶](#section-10.2.1-19.2){.pilcrow}
:   

Duplicate segments:
:   [Section
    2](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc5560#section-2){.relref} of
    \[[RFC5560](#RFC5560){.xref}\] defines identical packets and is
    suitable for evaluation of TCP packets to detect duplication.
    Observation of a segment duplicates a segment previously observed
    (and thus no corresponding observed segment gap) indicates loss on
    the path following the OP (e.g., the segment overlaps part of the
    octet stream already observed at the
    OP).[¶](#section-10.2.1-19.4){.pilcrow}
:   

Each observation of an out-of-order or duplicate segment infers a
singleton of loss, but the composition of round-trip loss counts will be
conducted over a measurement interval that is synonymous with a single
TCP connection.[¶](#section-10.2.1-20){.pilcrow}

With the above observations in the Forward direction over a measurement
interval, the count of out-of-order and duplicate segments is defined as
RTL_fwd. Comparable observations in the Reverse direction are defined as
RTL_rev.[¶](#section-10.2.1-21){.pilcrow}

For a measurement interval (corresponding to a single TCP connection) T0
to Tf, the [REQUIRED]{.bcp14} Composition Function for the two
single-direction counts of inferred loss
is:[¶](#section-10.2.1-22){.pilcrow}

RTLoss = RTL_fwd + RTL_rev[¶](#section-10.2.1-23){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#section-10.2.2 .section}
#### [10.2.2.](#section-10.2.2){.section-number .selfRef} [Fixed Parameters](#name-fixed-parameters-7){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-fixed-parameters-7}

[]{.break}

Traffic Filters:
:   []{.break}

    IPv4 header values:
    :   []{.break}

        DSCP:
        :   Set to 0[¶](#section-10.2.2-1.2.2.2.2.2){.pilcrow}
        :   

        Protocol:
        :   Set to 06 (TCP)[¶](#section-10.2.2-1.2.2.2.2.4){.pilcrow}
        :   
    :   

    []{.break}

    IPv6 header values:
    :   []{.break}

        DSCP:
        :   Set to 0[¶](#section-10.2.2-1.2.3.2.2.2){.pilcrow}
        :   

        Hop Count:
        :   Set to 255[¶](#section-10.2.2-1.2.3.2.2.4){.pilcrow}
        :   

        Next Header:
        :   Set to 6 (TCP)[¶](#section-10.2.2-1.2.3.2.2.6){.pilcrow}
        :   

        Flow Label:
        :   Set to 0[¶](#section-10.2.2-1.2.3.2.2.8){.pilcrow}
        :   

        Extension Headers:
        :   None[¶](#section-10.2.2-1.2.3.2.2.10){.pilcrow}
        :   
    :   

    []{.break}

    TCP header values:
    :   []{.break}

        Flags:
        :   ACK, SYN, FIN, set as
            required[¶](#section-10.2.2-1.2.4.2.2.2){.pilcrow}
        :   

        Timestamps Option (TSopt):
        :   Set.  See [Section
            3.2](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc7323#section-3.2){.relref}
            of
            \[[RFC7323](#RFC7323){.xref}\][¶](#section-10.2.2-1.2.4.2.2.4){.pilcrow}
        :   
    :   
:   
:::
:::

::: {#section-10.3 .section}
### [10.3.](#section-10.3){.section-number .selfRef} [Method of Measurement](#name-method-of-measurement-7){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-method-of-measurement-7}

This category includes columns for references to relevant sections of
the RFC(s) and any supplemental information needed to ensure an
unambiguous method for implementations.[¶](#section-10.3-1){.pilcrow}

::: {#ref-methods-10.3.1}
::: {#section-10.3.1 .section}
#### [10.3.1.](#section-10.3.1){.section-number .selfRef} [Reference Methods](#name-reference-methods-7){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-reference-methods-7}

The foundational methodology for this metric is defined in [Section
4](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc7323#section-4){.relref} of
\[[RFC7323](#RFC7323){.xref}\] using the Timestamps option with
modifications that allow application at a mid-path OP
\[[RFC7011](#RFC7011){.xref}\]. Further details and applicable
heuristics were derived from \[[Strowes](#Strowes){.xref}\] and
\[[Trammell-14](#Trammell-14){.xref}\].[¶](#section-10.3.1-1){.pilcrow}

The Traffic Filter at the OP is configured to observe a single TCP
connection. When the SYN/SYN-ACK/ACK handshake occurs, it offers the
first opportunity to measure both RTD_fwd (on the SYN to SYN-ACK pair)
and RTD_rev (on the SYN-ACK to ACK pair). Label this singleton of
RTDelay as RTDelay_HS (composed using the Forward and Reverse
measurement pair). RTDelay_HS [SHALL]{.bcp14} be treated separately from
other RTDelays on data-bearing packets and their ACKs. The RTDelay_HS
value [MAY]{.bcp14} be used as a consistency check on the composed
values of RTDelay for payload-bearing
packets.[¶](#section-10.3.1-2){.pilcrow}

For payload-bearing packets, the OP measures the time interval between
observation of a packet with sequence number \"s\" and the corresponding
ACK with the same sequence number. When the payload is transferred from
host A to host B, the observed interval is
RTD_fwd.[¶](#section-10.3.1-3){.pilcrow}

For payload-bearing packets, each observation of an out-of-order or
duplicate segment infers a loss count, but the composition of round-trip
loss counts will be conducted over a measurement interval that is
synonymous with a single TCP connection.[¶](#section-10.3.1-4){.pilcrow}

Because many data transfers are unidirectional (say, in the Forward
direction from host A to host B), it is necessary to use pure ACK
packets with Timestamp (TSval) and packets with the Timestamp value echo
to perform a RTD_rev measurement. The time interval between observation
of the ACK from B to A, and the Corresponding Packet with a Timestamp
Echo Reply (TSecr) field \[[RFC7323](#RFC7323){.xref}\], is the
RTD_rev.[¶](#section-10.3.1-5){.pilcrow}

Delay Measurement Filtering Heuristics:[¶](#section-10.3.1-6){.pilcrow}

-   [If data payloads were transferred in both Forward and Reverse
    directions, then the Round-Trip Time Measurement rule in [Section
    4.1](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc7323#section-4.1){.relref} of
    \[[RFC7323](#RFC7323){.xref}\] could be applied. This rule
    essentially excludes any measurement using a packet unless it makes
    progress in the transfer (advances the left edge of the send window,
    consistent with
    \[[Strowes](#Strowes){.xref}\]).[¶](#section-10.3.1-7.1){.pilcrow}]{#section-10.3.1-7.1}
-   [A different heuristic from \[[Trammell-14](#Trammell-14){.xref}\]
    is to exclude any RTD_rev that is larger than previously observed
    values. This would tend to exclude Reverse measurements taken when
    the application has no data ready to send, because considerable time
    could be added to RTD_rev from this source of
    error.[¶](#section-10.3.1-7.2){.pilcrow}]{#section-10.3.1-7.2}
-   [Note that the above heuristic assumes that host A is sending data.
    Host A expecting a download would mean that this heuristic should be
    applied to
    RTD_fwd.[¶](#section-10.3.1-7.3){.pilcrow}]{#section-10.3.1-7.3}
-   [The statistic calculations to summarize the delay (RTDelay)
    [SHALL]{.bcp14} be performed on the conditional distribution,
    conditioned on successful Forward and Reverse measurements that
    follow the
    heuristics.[¶](#section-10.3.1-7.4){.pilcrow}]{#section-10.3.1-7.4}

Method for Inferring Loss:[¶](#section-10.3.1-8){.pilcrow}

-   [The OP tracks sequence numbers and stores gaps for each direction
    of transmission, as well as the next expected sequence number as
    discussed in \[[Trammell-14](#Trammell-14){.xref}\] and
    \[[RFC4737](#RFC4737){.xref}\]. Loss is inferred from out-of-order
    segments and duplicate
    segments.[¶](#section-10.3.1-9.1){.pilcrow}]{#section-10.3.1-9.1}

Loss Measurement Filtering Heuristics:[¶](#section-10.3.1-10){.pilcrow}

-   [\[[Trammell-14](#Trammell-14){.xref}\] adds a window of evaluation
    based on the
    RTDelay.[¶](#section-10.3.1-11.1){.pilcrow}]{#section-10.3.1-11.1}
-   [Distinguish reordered packets from out-of-order segments due to
    loss, because the sequence number gap is filled during the same
    RTDelay window. Segments detected as reordered according to
    \[[RFC4737](#RFC4737){.xref}\] [MUST]{.bcp14} reduce the loss count
    inferred from out-of-order
    segments.[¶](#section-10.3.1-11.2){.pilcrow}]{#section-10.3.1-11.2}
-   [Spurious (unneeded) retransmissions (observed as duplicates) can
    also be reduced in this way, as described in
    \[[Trammell-14](#Trammell-14){.xref}\].[¶](#section-10.3.1-11.3){.pilcrow}]{#section-10.3.1-11.3}

Sources of Error:[¶](#section-10.3.1-12){.pilcrow}

-   [The principal source of RTDelay error is the host processing time
    to return a packet that defines the termination of a time interval.
    The heuristics above intend to mitigate these errors by excluding
    measurements where host processing time is a significant part of
    RTD_fwd or
    RTD_rev.[¶](#section-10.3.1-13.1){.pilcrow}]{#section-10.3.1-13.1}
-   [A key source of RTLoss error is observation loss, as described in
    Section 3 of
    \[[Trammell-14](#Trammell-14){.xref}\].[¶](#section-10.3.1-13.2){.pilcrow}]{#section-10.3.1-13.2}
:::
:::

::: {#section-10.3.2 .section}
#### [10.3.2.](#section-10.3.2){.section-number .selfRef} [Packet Stream Generation](#name-packet-stream-generation-7){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-packet-stream-generation-7}

N/A[¶](#section-10.3.2-1){.pilcrow}
:::

::: {#section-10.3.3 .section}
#### [10.3.3.](#section-10.3.3){.section-number .selfRef} [Traffic Filtering (Observation) Details](#name-traffic-filtering-observation-det){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-traffic-filtering-observation-det}

The Fixed Parameters above give a portion of the Traffic Filter. Other
aspects will be supplied as Runtime Parameters
(below).[¶](#section-10.3.3-1){.pilcrow}
:::

::: {#section-10.3.4 .section}
#### [10.3.4.](#section-10.3.4){.section-number .selfRef} [Sampling Distribution](#name-sampling-distribution-7){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-sampling-distribution-7}

This metric requires a complete sample of all packets that qualify
according to the Traffic Filter
criteria.[¶](#section-10.3.4-1){.pilcrow}
:::

::: {#section-10.3.5 .section}
#### [10.3.5.](#section-10.3.5){.section-number .selfRef} [Runtime Parameters and Data Format](#name-runtime-parameters-and-data-forma){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-runtime-parameters-and-data-forma}

Runtime Parameters are input factors that must be determined, configured
into the measurement system, and reported with the results for the
context to be complete.[¶](#section-10.3.5-1){.pilcrow}

[]{.break}

Src:
:   The IP address of the host in the host A Role (format
    ipv4‑address-no-zone value for IPv4 or ipv6-address-no-zone value
    for IPv6; see [Section
    4](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6991#section-4){.relref} of
    \[[RFC6991](#RFC6991){.xref}\]).[¶](#section-10.3.5-2.2){.pilcrow}
:   

Dst:
:   The IP address of the host in the host B Role (format
    ipv4‑address-no-zone value for IPv4 or ipv6-address-no-zone value
    for IPv6; see [Section
    4](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6991#section-4){.relref} of
    \[[RFC6991](#RFC6991){.xref}\]).[¶](#section-10.3.5-2.4){.pilcrow}
:   

T0:
:   A time, the start of a measurement interval (format \"date‑time\" as
    specified in [Section
    5.6](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc3339#section-5.6){.relref} of
    \[[RFC3339](#RFC3339){.xref}\]; see also \"date‑and‑time\" in
    [Section
    3](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6991#section-3){.relref} of
    \[[RFC6991](#RFC6991){.xref}\]). The UTC Time Zone is required by
    [Section
    6.1](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc2330#section-6.1){.relref} of
    \[[RFC2330](#RFC2330){.xref}\]. When T0 is \"all-zeros\", a start
    time is unspecified and Tf is to be interpreted as the duration of
    the measurement interval. The start time is controlled through other
    means.[¶](#section-10.3.5-2.6){.pilcrow}
:   

Tf:
:   Optionally, the end of a measurement interval (format \"date‑time\"
    as specified in [Section
    5.6](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc3339#section-5.6){.relref} of
    \[[RFC3339](#RFC3339){.xref}\]; see also \"date‑and‑time\" in
    [Section
    3](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6991#section-3){.relref} of
    \[[RFC6991](#RFC6991){.xref}\]), or the duration (see T0). The UTC
    Time Zone is required by [Section
    6.1](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc2330#section-6.1){.relref} of
    \[[RFC2330](#RFC2330){.xref}\]. Alternatively, the end of the
    measurement interval [MAY]{.bcp14} be controlled by the measured
    connection, where the second pair of FIN and ACK packets exchanged
    between host A and host B effectively ends the
    interval.[¶](#section-10.3.5-2.8){.pilcrow}
:   

TTL or Hop Limit:
:   Set at desired value.[¶](#section-10.3.5-2.10){.pilcrow}
:   
:::

::: {#section-10.3.6 .section}
#### [10.3.6.](#section-10.3.6){.section-number .selfRef} [Roles](#name-roles-7){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-roles-7}

[]{.break}

host A:
:   Launches the SYN packet to open the connection. The Role of \"host
    A\" is synonymous with the IP address used at host
    A.[¶](#section-10.3.6-1.2){.pilcrow}
:   

host B:
:   Replies with the SYN-ACK packet to open the connection. The Role of
    \"host B\" is synonymous with the IP address used at host
    B.[¶](#section-10.3.6-1.4){.pilcrow}
:   
:::
:::

::: {#section-10.4 .section}
### [10.4.](#section-10.4){.section-number .selfRef} [Output](#name-output-7){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-output-7}

This category specifies all details of the output of measurements using
the metric.[¶](#section-10.4-1){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-10.4.1 .section}
#### [10.4.1.](#section-10.4.1){.section-number .selfRef} [Type](#name-type-7){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-type-7}

RTDelay Types are discussed in the subsections
below.[¶](#section-10.4.1-1){.pilcrow}

For RTLoss: The count of lost packets.[¶](#section-10.4.1-2){.pilcrow}
:::

::: {#section-10.4.2 .section}
#### [10.4.2.](#section-10.4.2){.section-number .selfRef} [Reference Definition](#name-reference-definition-14){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-reference-definition-14}

For all output types:[¶](#section-10.4.2-1){.pilcrow}

[]{.break}

T0:
:   The start of a measurement interval (format \"date‑time\" as
    specified in [Section
    5.6](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc3339#section-5.6){.relref} of
    \[[RFC3339](#RFC3339){.xref}\]; see also \"date‑and‑time\" in
    [Section
    3](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6991#section-3){.relref} of
    \[[RFC6991](#RFC6991){.xref}\]). The UTC Time Zone is required by
    [Section
    6.1](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc2330#section-6.1){.relref} of
    \[[RFC2330](#RFC2330){.xref}\].[¶](#section-10.4.2-2.2){.pilcrow}
:   

Tf:
:   The end of a measurement interval (format \"date‑time\" as specified
    in [Section
    5.6](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc3339#section-5.6){.relref} of
    \[[RFC3339](#RFC3339){.xref}\]; see also \"date‑and‑time\" in
    [Section
    3](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6991#section-3){.relref} of
    \[[RFC6991](#RFC6991){.xref}\]). The UTC Time Zone is required by
    [Section
    6.1](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc2330#section-6.1){.relref} of
    \[[RFC2330](#RFC2330){.xref}\]. The end of the measurement interval
    [MAY]{.bcp14} be controlled by the measured connection, where the
    second pair of FIN and ACK packets exchanged between host A and host
    B effectively ends the interval.[¶](#section-10.4.2-2.4){.pilcrow}
:   

RTDelay_Passive_IP-TCP-HS:
:   The round-trip delay of the handshake is a
    Singleton.[¶](#section-10.4.2-2.6){.pilcrow}
:   

RTLoss:
:   The count of lost packets.[¶](#section-10.4.2-2.8){.pilcrow}
:   

For each \<statistic>, Singleton, or Loss Count, one of the following
subsections applies.[¶](#section-10.4.2-3){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-10.4.2.1 .section}
##### [10.4.2.1.](#section-10.4.2.1){.section-number .selfRef} [Mean](#name-mean-4){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-mean-4}

The mean [SHALL]{.bcp14} be calculated using the conditional
distribution of all packets with a finite value of round-trip delay
(undefined delays are excluded) \-- a single value, as
follows:[¶](#section-10.4.2.1-1){.pilcrow}

See [Section
4.1](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc3393#section-4.1){.relref} of
\[[RFC3393](#RFC3393){.xref}\] for details on the conditional
distribution to exclude undefined values of delay, and see [Section
5](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6703#section-5){.relref} of
\[[RFC6703](#RFC6703){.xref}\] for background on this analysis
choice.[¶](#section-10.4.2.1-2){.pilcrow}

See [Section
4.2.2](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6049#section-4.2.2){.relref} of
\[[RFC6049](#RFC6049){.xref}\] for details on calculating this
statistic; see also [Section
4.2.3](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6049#section-4.2.3){.relref} of
\[[RFC6049](#RFC6049){.xref}\].[¶](#section-10.4.2.1-3){.pilcrow}

[]{.break}

Mean:
:   The time value of the result is expressed in units of seconds, as a
    positive value of type decimal64 with fraction digits = 9 (see
    [Section
    9.3](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6020#section-9.3){.relref} of
    \[[RFC6020](#RFC6020){.xref}\]) with a resolution of
    0.000000001 seconds (1.0 ns), and with lossless conversion to/from
    the 64-bit NTP timestamp as per [Section
    6](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc5905#section-6){.relref} of
    \[[RFC5905](#RFC5905){.xref}\].[¶](#section-10.4.2.1-4.2){.pilcrow}
:   
:::

::: {#section-10.4.2.2 .section}
##### [10.4.2.2.](#section-10.4.2.2){.section-number .selfRef} [Min](#name-min-4){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-min-4}

The minimum [SHALL]{.bcp14} be calculated using the conditional
distribution of all packets with a finite value of round-trip delay
(undefined delays are excluded) \-- a single value, as
follows:[¶](#section-10.4.2.2-1){.pilcrow}

See [Section
4.1](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc3393#section-4.1){.relref} of
\[[RFC3393](#RFC3393){.xref}\] for details on the conditional
distribution to exclude undefined values of delay, and see [Section
5](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6703#section-5){.relref} of
\[[RFC6703](#RFC6703){.xref}\] for background on this analysis
choice.[¶](#section-10.4.2.2-2){.pilcrow}

See [Section
4.3.2](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6049#section-4.3.2){.relref} of
\[[RFC6049](#RFC6049){.xref}\] for details on calculating this
statistic; see also [Section
4.3.3](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6049#section-4.3.3){.relref} of
\[[RFC6049](#RFC6049){.xref}\].[¶](#section-10.4.2.2-3){.pilcrow}

[]{.break}

Min:
:   The time value of the result is expressed in units of seconds, as a
    positive value of type decimal64 with fraction digits = 9 (see
    [Section
    9.3](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6020#section-9.3){.relref} of
    \[[RFC6020](#RFC6020){.xref}\]) with a resolution of
    0.000000001 seconds (1.0 ns), and with lossless conversion to/from
    the 64-bit NTP timestamp as per [Section
    6](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc5905#section-6){.relref} of
    \[[RFC5905](#RFC5905){.xref}\].[¶](#section-10.4.2.2-4.2){.pilcrow}
:   
:::

::: {#section-10.4.2.3 .section}
##### [10.4.2.3.](#section-10.4.2.3){.section-number .selfRef} [Max](#name-max-4){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-max-4}

The maximum [SHALL]{.bcp14} be calculated using the conditional
distribution of all packets with a finite value of round-trip delay
(undefined delays are excluded) \-- a single value, as
follows:[¶](#section-10.4.2.3-1){.pilcrow}

See [Section
4.1](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc3393#section-4.1){.relref} of
\[[RFC3393](#RFC3393){.xref}\] for details on the conditional
distribution to exclude undefined values of delay, and see [Section
5](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6703#section-5){.relref} of
\[[RFC6703](#RFC6703){.xref}\] for background on this analysis
choice.[¶](#section-10.4.2.3-2){.pilcrow}

See [Section
4.3.2](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6049#section-4.3.2){.relref} of
\[[RFC6049](#RFC6049){.xref}\] for a closely related method for
calculating this statistic; see also [Section
4.3.3](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6049#section-4.3.3){.relref} of
\[[RFC6049](#RFC6049){.xref}\]. The formula is as
follows:[¶](#section-10.4.2.3-3){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-10.4.2.3-4 .alignLeft .art-text .artwork}
       Max = (FiniteDelay[j])

[¶](#section-10.4.2.3-4){.pilcrow}
:::

-   [such that for some index, j, where 1 \<= j \<= N
    FiniteDelay\[j\] >= FiniteDelay\[n\] for all
    n[¶](#section-10.4.2.3-5.1){.pilcrow}]{#section-10.4.2.3-5.1}

[]{.break}

Max:
:   The time value of the result is expressed in units of seconds, as a
    positive value of type decimal64 with fraction digits = 9 (see
    [Section
    9.3](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6020#section-9.3){.relref} of
    \[[RFC6020](#RFC6020){.xref}\]) with a resolution of
    0.000000001 seconds (1.0 ns), and with lossless conversion to/from
    the 64-bit NTP timestamp as per [Section
    6](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc5905#section-6){.relref} of
    \[[RFC5905](#RFC5905){.xref}\].[¶](#section-10.4.2.3-6.2){.pilcrow}
:   
:::

::: {#section-10.4.2.4 .section}
##### [10.4.2.4.](#section-10.4.2.4){.section-number .selfRef} [Singleton](#name-singleton){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-singleton}

The singleton [SHALL]{.bcp14} be calculated using the successful RTD_fwd
(on the SYN to SYN-ACK pair) and RTD_rev (on the SYN-ACK to ACK pair),
see [Section
10.3.1](#ref-methods-10.3.1){.xref}.[¶](#section-10.4.2.4-1){.pilcrow}

The singleton time value of the result is expressed in units of seconds,
as a positive value of type decimal64 with fraction digits = 9 (see
[Section
9.3](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6020#section-9.3){.relref} of
\[[RFC6020](#RFC6020){.xref}\]) with resolution of 0.000000001 seconds
(1.0 ns), and with lossless conversion to/from the 64-bit NTP timestamp
as per [Section
6](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc5905#section-6){.relref} of
\[[RFC5905](#RFC5905){.xref}\].[¶](#section-10.4.2.4-2){.pilcrow}
:::

::: {#section-10.4.2.5 .section}
##### [10.4.2.5.](#section-10.4.2.5){.section-number .selfRef} [Loss Counts](#name-loss-counts){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-loss-counts}

RTLoss_Passive_IP-TCP_RFC8912sec10_Packet_Count: The count of lost
packets.[¶](#section-10.4.2.5-1){.pilcrow}

Observation of an out-of-order segment or duplicate segment infers a
loss count, after application of the Definitions of [Section
10.2.1](#s10.2.1){.xref} and the Loss Measurement Filtering Heuristics
of [Section 10.3.1](#ref-methods-10.3.1){.xref}. The composition of
round-trip loss counts will be conducted over a measurement interval
that is synonymous with a single TCP
connection.[¶](#section-10.4.2.5-2){.pilcrow}

For a measurement interval (corresponding to a single TCP connection) T0
to Tf, the [REQUIRED]{.bcp14} Composition Function for the two single-
direction counts of inferred loss is:[¶](#section-10.4.2.5-3){.pilcrow}

RTLoss = RTL_fwd + RTL_rev[¶](#section-10.4.2.5-4){.pilcrow}

[]{.break}

Packet count:
:   The numeric value of the result is expressed in units of lost
    packets, as a positive value of type uint64 (represents integer
    values between 0 and 18446744073709551615, inclusively (see [Section
    9.2](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6020#section-9.2){.relref} of
    \[[RFC6020](#RFC6020){.xref}\]).[¶](#section-10.4.2.5-5.2){.pilcrow}
:   
:::
:::

::: {#section-10.4.3 .section}
#### [10.4.3.](#section-10.4.3){.section-number .selfRef} [Metric Units](#name-metric-units-7){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-metric-units-7}

The \<statistic> of round-trip delay is expressed in seconds, where
\<statistic> is one of:[¶](#section-10.4.3-1){.pilcrow}

-   [Mean[¶](#section-10.4.3-2.1){.pilcrow}]{#section-10.4.3-2.1}
-   [Min[¶](#section-10.4.3-2.2){.pilcrow}]{#section-10.4.3-2.2}
-   [Max[¶](#section-10.4.3-2.3){.pilcrow}]{#section-10.4.3-2.3}

The round-trip delay of the TCP handshake singleton is expressed in
seconds.[¶](#section-10.4.3-3){.pilcrow}

The round-trip loss count is expressed as a number of
packets.[¶](#section-10.4.3-4){.pilcrow}
:::

::: {#section-10.4.4 .section}
#### [10.4.4.](#section-10.4.4){.section-number .selfRef} [Calibration](#name-calibration-7){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-calibration-7}

Passive Measurements at an OP could be calibrated against an Active
Measurement (with loss emulation) at host A or host B, where the Active
Measurement represents the ground truth.[¶](#section-10.4.4-1){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#section-11 .section}
## [11.](#section-11){.section-number .selfRef} [Security Considerations](#name-security-considerations){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-security-considerations}

These Registry Entries represent no known implications for Internet
security. With the exception of \[[RFC1035](#RFC1035){.xref}\], each RFC
referenced above contains a Security Considerations section. Further,
the Large-scale Measurement of Broadband Performance (LMAP) framework
\[[RFC7594](#RFC7594){.xref}\] provides both security and privacy
considerations for measurements.[¶](#section-11-1){.pilcrow}

There are potential privacy considerations for observed traffic,
particularly for Passive Metrics as discussed in [Section
10](#tcp-rt-delay-loss-reg-entries){.xref}. An attacker that knows that
its TCP connection is being measured can modify its behavior to skew the
measurement results.[¶](#section-11-2){.pilcrow}
:::

::: {#IANA}
::: {#section-12 .section}
## [12.](#section-12){.section-number .selfRef} [IANA Considerations](#name-iana-considerations){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-iana-considerations}

IANA has populated the Performance Metrics Registry defined in
\[[RFC8911](#RFC8911){.xref}\] with the values defined in
Sections [4](#udp-rt-latency-loss-reg-entries){.xref} through
[10](#tcp-rt-delay-loss-reg-entries){.xref}.[¶](#section-12-1){.pilcrow}

See the IANA Considerations section of \[[RFC8911](#RFC8911){.xref}\]
for additional considerations.[¶](#section-12-2){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

    [Eardley, P.]{.refAuthor}, [Morton, A.]{.refAuthor}, and [A.
    Akhter]{.refAuthor}, [\"Registry for Performance
    Metrics\"]{.refTitle}, [RFC 8911]{.seriesInfo}, [DOI
    10.17487/RFC8911]{.seriesInfo}, November 2021,
    \<<https://www.rfc-editor.org/info/rfc8911>\>.
:   

\[Strowes\]
:   [Strowes, S.]{.refAuthor}, [\"Passively Measuring TCP Round-Trip
    Times\"]{.refTitle}, [Communications of the ACM, Vol. 56 No. 10,
    Pages 57-64]{.refContent}, [DOI
    10.1145/2507771.2507781]{.seriesInfo}, October 2013,
    \<<https://dl.acm.org/doi/10.1145/2507771.2507781>\>.
:   

\[Trammell-14\]
:   [Trammell, B.]{.refAuthor}, [Gugelmann, D.]{.refAuthor}, and [N.
    Brownlee]{.refAuthor}, [\"Inline Data Integrity Signals for Passive
    Measurement\"]{.refTitle}, [In: Dainotti A., Mahanti A., Uhlig S.
    (eds) Traffic Monitoring and Analysis. TMA 2014. Lecture Notes in
    Computer Science, vol 8406. Springer, Berlin,
    Heidelberg]{.refContent}, [DOI
    10.1007/978-3-642-54999-1_2]{.seriesInfo}, March 2014,
    \<<https://link.springer.com/chapter/10.1007/978-3-642-54999-1_2>\>.
:

::: {#appendix-A .section}
## [Acknowledgments](#name-acknowledgments){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-acknowledgments}

The authors thank [Brian Trammell]{.contact-name} for suggesting the
term \"Runtime Parameters\", which led to the distinction between
Runtime and Fixed Parameters implemented in this memo, for identifying
the IP Flow Information Export (IPFIX) metric with Flow Key as an
example, for suggesting the Passive TCP RTD Metric and supporting
references, and for many other productive suggestions. Thanks to [Peter
Koch]{.contact-name}, who provided several useful suggestions for
disambiguating successive DNS queries in the DNS Response time
metric.[¶](#appendix-A-1){.pilcrow}

The authors also acknowledge the constructive reviews and helpful
suggestions from [Barbara Stark]{.contact-name}, [Juergen
Schoenwaelder]{.contact-name}, [Tim Carey]{.contact-name}, [Yaakov
Stein]{.contact-name}, and participants in the LMAP Working Group.
Thanks to [Michelle Cotton]{.contact-name} for her early IANA reviews,
and to [Amanda Baber]{.contact-name} for answering questions related to
the presentation of the Registry and accessibility of the complete
template via URL.[¶](#appendix-A-2){.pilcrow}
:::
